Wuhan River Water Gradually Recedes

The Water Conservancy Bureau Plans to Repair Breached Dikes

The Garrison Command Advances Curfew Hours

Hankou Correspondence: This year's flood is extraordinarily severe, with dikes in all of Hubei collapsing entirely, and the dikes themselves largely submerged. The autumn waters stretch endlessly, all a single color, making it impossible to distinguish between river and land. Now, as the waters gradually recede, traces of the submerged dikes are slowly becoming visible. The Water Conservancy Bureau is undertaking surveys and planning the repair of breaches in the dikes, and will raise substantial funds to heighten the dikes, as a permanent solution. The first step is to survey the Zhanggong Dike in Hankou, the Wufeng Dike in Wuchang, and the Wujin Dike. The second step is to survey the main dikes along the Xiang River. The third step is to survey the dikes along the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The first step is now complete and work has started on surveying the main dikes along both banks of the Xiang River. Once the survey is complete, repairs will begin. According to Bureau Director Chen Keming, it is estimated that it will cost three million yuan to fill the breaches in the dikes. If all the main dikes in the province are to be raised and thickened, the cost would be over forty million yuan. Given the financial exhaustion of Hubei Province, it is feared that only the breaches can be repaired; a fundamental solution will have to wait for the future.

Wuhan has been flooded for more than forty days. Due to the strict precautions taken by the garrison troops, order has been maintained. Now that the floodwaters are gradually receding, defense remains crucial. The Garrison Command has deployed a network of sentries around Wuhan and has ordered the full mobilization of the Water Police Bureau for patrols, with two large boats provided by the Command to assist in patrolling. The Xiang River has been temporarily blockaded and random checks are being carried out on the streets. Furthermore, a notice was issued today (the 16th) advancing the curfew to start on the 20th. Traffic will be cut off at 10:00 PM every night. Government employees traveling on official business will not be able to pass without a pass issued by the Command. The notice is recorded below: 1. Since the flooding of Wuhan, this Command has implemented a special curfew, from 10:00 PM each night to 5:00 AM the next morning, deploying sentries throughout the Wuhan garrison area and along the outer lines, cutting off traffic. However, government and military personnel wearing badges or emblems, or able to give the correct password, were granted permission to pass. Recently, as the city streets have become passable, the curfew has been tightened. At the 73rd Garrison Conference on September 2nd, the chairman raised the issue for discussion. Although there are many disaster victims and order is disrupted after the city is flooded, the inconvenience of transportation and difficulty of movement actually reduce concerns about the defense area. Therefore, cutting off traffic at night, not issuing passes, and only having special permission to pass, based on the symbols or badges of government and military units, or the ability to give the correct password, was sufficient to avoid negligence. As the waters recede, the situation will be more serious than during the flooding. In addition to all garrison-related tasks being tightened in comparison to the flooding, cutting off traffic at night without issuing passes will not be strict or effective. Military and police personnel will also find it difficult to cut off traffic. Should passes be issued for cutting off traffic at night after the waters recede? This is submitted for public decision. After unanimous resolution, the Command will issue passes according to the established rules of last year, in order to strictly maintain the garrison, and to cut off traffic from 11:00 PM each night, etc., as recorded. It was also recorded and submitted to the Land, Sea, and Air Force General Command for instruction Deputy Character No. 982, which stated: "Received the submission and approve the issuance of passes in accordance with the resolution to facilitate strict inspection and prevent wrongdoing. This order is for your information." Subsequently, Instruction No. 2315 was received, ordering that the time for cutting off traffic at night, as recorded in the conference report, should still be changed to start at 10:00 PM each night, etc. It is now decided that starting from September 20th, traffic will be cut off every night from 10:00 PM, and no one will be allowed to pass without holding a newly colored pass issued by this Command. All blue passes issued last year are no longer valid and are hereby canceled. All military unit personnel with complete badges who are out on official business must also wait to give the password and have their passes checked before being allowed to pass. As for the cars of government and military personnel, they must display clear badges or flags of their respective agencies in front of the car after traffic is cut off at night, and slow down and stop when approaching a sentry post, waiting for the sentry to inquire about the password, ask questions clearly, or check the pass before passing. In addition to separate letters, this notice is hereby issued for general information. (July 16th)

Inspection Record of the Disaster Situation in Hubei Province (1)

Reports from Relief Teams One and Two

Hankou Correspondence: In order to provide extensive relief in light of the vast disaster areas and the large number of disaster victims in various counties in Hubei, the Hubei Flood Relief Association, together with the Central Health Group's Hankou Office, the North China Famine Relief Association, the Northeast Four Provinces Charity Federation, the Universal Morality Society, the Chinese Jishi Society, and the China General Society of the World Red Cross Relief Team, and other organizations, have organized relief teams to set out in different directions. The first team, led by Yang Zigong, set out for Xindi. The second team, led by Du Yannian, set out for Fankou, as the disaster situation there is the most serious, and relief cannot be delayed. Both teams have now arrived at their destinations and are providing relief. They have already sent letters to the Relief Association, reporting on the disaster situation, detailing the suffering of the refugees. The information obtained from on-the-spot investigations is credible and reliable, and is introduced as follows:

Xindi: The first relief team, led by Yang Zigong, Chairman of the Northeast Four Provinces Charity Federation, and Nie Youxun, Director of the Disaster Area Working Group of the National Government Relief Committee, and other team members, carrying 495 bags of white rice, 5,000 bags of flour, and medical supplies, set off from Hankou on the Wanxing Wheel to the west. They docked at Xiaojinkou at 7:00 PM. On the morning of the 9th, they sailed from Jinkou, passing through various places such as Shaomaoshan, Dazui, Donggelao, and Dengjiakou, and arrived at Paizhou at 12:00 PM and Jiayu at 5:00 PM. Because Baotazhou was known as a den of thieves, they were unable to proceed and docked there. On the morning of the 10th, at 4:00 AM, they sailed from Jiayu, passing through Liuzikou, arriving at Baotazhou at 5:00 AM, and at Lujiakou at 8:30 AM. Suddenly, gunfire erupted, shooting at the Wanxing Wheel and the Parrot Wheel transporting rice. They opened up full power and sped upwards, finally arriving safely at Xindi after more than an hour. From Hankou to here, the journey was more than 360 miles. The floodwaters were surging, a vast expanse of water. Paizhou was affected by the Jiangwan, and the disaster situation was particularly serious. The situation in Jinkou was roughly the same. After the staff arrived in Xindi, their shock subsided. They immediately convened a joint meeting of various agencies and organizations at Xingang near the port that evening to discuss inspecting the true situation of the disaster victims and carrying out a household survey. The main decisions were: 1. Relief area: From Zhujiafeng in Houping Township in the upper reaches to Fanjiuzhou in Maobu Township in the lower reaches, and to Yangjiazu in Xuping Township in the inner river, a total of more than 50 li from east to west and 10 li from north to south. 2. Survey method: The team members will work with local organizations to convene the Pao-Tung and Chia-Chang of the various disaster areas to conduct detailed surveys, limited to the poor and orphaned. Those under 12 years old are counted as small households, and those over 12 years old are counted as large households. The survey must be completed within three days. 3. Relief distribution method: First, relief tickets will be issued, specifying the date and location for distribution, and distribution will be carried out under the maintenance of order by the military and police. On the morning of the 11th, at 8:00 AM, they met with the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, and others to investigate the disaster situation in the lower townships, passing through the Old Coffin Temple, Maopu Township, Yejiuzhou, Wangjiuzhou, Hujiuzhou, and Ganjiuzhou, with an estimated 2,000 disaster victims. On the morning of the 12th, at 8:00 AM, they investigated the Zhujiazu area in the upper townships. In this area, seven or eight sections of the street embankment were broken by the water, the widest being more than six zhang. A large number of houses collapsed. In summary, all the places inspected had become a land of water, with fields and houses submerged in water. Most of the disaster victims along the river were crowded on the dikes that had not collapsed, with thatched sheds lined up one after another, resembling villages. Those living in the open air accounted for two or three tenths. There were also entire families living on boats, who had not had a full meal for several days. In the inner river areas, due to the lack of dikes and hills, many disaster victims lived in the houses that had been submerged but had not collapsed, living on wooden frames. Others built nests in trees, and their remaining belongings were placed on the roofs. The tragedy of the disaster is truly rare. The team is now providing relief and is scheduled to complete its work within three days and return to Hankou before the 20th.

Fankou: The second relief team, led by Du Yannian and Qian Jinjian, left Hankou on the 11th and went east to Fankou, which belongs to Echeng, to provide relief to the refugees. They arrived in Echeng at noon and contacted the chairman of the County Chamber of Commerce and the head of the Security Regiment to agree to divide into 20 groups and go to the places where the disaster victims were gathered to conduct detailed surveys. In the afternoon, they inspected various places inside and outside the county seat, which were deeply flooded. The disaster victims were crowded on the city walls, and their state of hunger and cold was too terrible to behold. On the morning of the 12th, the ship sailed directly to Fankou, which is five li from the city and has the most serious disaster situation. The disaster victims were all camping on the nearby mountains. Although they were barely surviving, they were spared from drowning, but they were exposed to the wind and rain and could not withstand hunger and cold, which was also very sad. As for the disaster victims' households, according to the team's survey results, there are a total of more than 331,000 people in the county, of whom more than 138,000 are living in temples and ancestral halls, and building straw sheds in the open air, and are truly homeless. More than 83,000 people are in urgent need of relief. 318,146 mu of farmland have been flooded, and there is no harvest of early and late rice. About 5% of the elevated areas yielded crops, and about 2% or 3% of buckwheat. (September 16th)

Jiujiang Disaster Victims Cry Out in Hunger and Cold

Disaster Victims Number Over 150,000

Relief Funds are Few and Far Between

Refugee Shelters Have Not Been Implemented

Jiujiang Correspondence: In nearly a hundred years, Jiujiang has only experienced four major floods. The first time was in the fourth year of the Guangxu reign, the second time was in the twenty-seventh year of the Guangxu reign, and the third time was in the fifteenth year of the Republic of China. The highest water level of these three major floods was 44 chi and 9 cun. The dike collapses all occurred in the early sixth lunar month. The water began to recede a few days before the White Dew solar term, and could be completely receded within half a month after the Mid-Autumn Festival. Farmers could still replant, and the number of casualties and collapsed houses was also extremely limited. However, the scale of this flood and the magnitude of the losses are not only unprecedented, but also unheard of. At its highest point, the water level reached 45 chi and 5 cun, creating an unprecedented new record. The White Dew solar term has passed several days, and the river water is still rising and falling intermittently. It has never fallen to 45 chi. According to old farmers, if the water rises during the White Dew solar term, it will be difficult to recede during the heavy snow season. This means that there is no hope for winter crops this year, and no harvest can be expected for the next season. The number of people drowned exceeds 2,000, and floating corpses are still being discovered in the river. The value of the property lost is in the millions. It will be difficult to restore the area to its former state within ten years. In previous floods, disaster victims could still flee to other places to survive. This year, however, there were major floods everywhere. Those who fled to Anhui traveled through several counties for several days without getting a single meal. There was no way forward and no way back. More than half of the refugees died of starvation or disease. Some were so angry that they committed suicide by drowning, hanging themselves, or strangling themselves. In the past few days, the Jiujiang authorities have finally started to build sheds in preparation for taking in refugees, and the disaster victims have returned in droves. However, their number is less than half of what it was when they left. Those who fled to Nanchang have been temporarily taken in by the Provincial Relief Association, and the Department of Civil Affairs has ordered the Jiujiang County Government to send personnel to bring them back as soon as possible. It also ordered the suspension of issuing passports to refugees seeking food outside, and immediately recalled those that had already been issued. Although the orders have been issued, the disaster victims are unwilling to sit and wait for death. Therefore, in the past week, according to the provincial newspaper, more than a thousand people have still fled to Nanchang. In total, more than 25,000 people have been issued passports by the County Government to seek food outside. More than 16,000 people are scattered in the Xun city. These more than 40,000 disaster victims are mostly people from Fengkuo Township in the ninth district north of the Yangtze River, which is closer to Xun. The remaining disaster victims in Sangluo Township in the eighth district north of the Yangtze River, which is closer to Hukou and Pengze, and Chisong Township in the seventh district south of the Yangtze River, which is closer to the second, fourth, fifth, and sixth districts of Jiujiang County, are only relying on surplus grain and seeds to satisfy their hunger. The rural order is extremely chaotic, and the official authorities cannot maintain it. Looking to the future, one cannot help but feel apprehensive. In addition, there are more than 100,000 disaster victims who still have surplus grain and seeds, so they are still living in sheds and tents on the dikes, eating one meal of porridge every day or every other day. If there is no assistance after another month and a half, the food supply will also be exhausted.

The progress of relief efforts is rather slow. For example, Liu Zhi first donated 5,000 yuan in cash to relieve the disaster in Gan, which was allocated by the provincial government. Jiujiang received 600 yuan. This 600 yuan has not yet been distributed today. Furthermore, the Relief Association resolved to allocate 3,000 yuan in silver dollars to Jiujiang for emergency relief. The notification of this 3,000 yuan has only allowed the Nanchang Chamber of Commerce to pledge 900 yuan. In addition, 1,900 yuan has been raised from various places. Since the disaster began on August 1st, it has been more than a month and a half, and only 2,800 yuan in relief funds has been received. Using this to provide relief to more than 150,000 disaster victims is truly a drop in the bucket.

The temporary pledge of plowing cattle has been established, and its fund is 2,000 yuan. This 2,000 yuan is also allocated from the 2,800 yuan in relief funds. Currently, more than 200 plowing cattle have been collected, but due to poor management, more than half have died. Zhou Baipeng, a member of the National Government's Water Disaster Relief Committee, came to Xun to inspect and was very disapproving. He then joined Jiang Qun and other members of the Jiujiang Water Disaster Relief and Recovery Association (now renamed the Water Disaster Relief Committee) to select four locations: Lianhuadong, Shilipu, Gaochangmiao, and Mao Shanqi Tou, to set up cattle sheds to avoid the outbreak of cattle epidemics. However, due to the continuous rain, it has not been possible to start building the sheds.

Regarding the distribution of porridge, there was no order before August 29th. Some people received porridge tickets for five or six people, while others could not get a single ticket for five or six people. The Relief and Recovery Association discovered this problem and convened the disaster victims at the Dajiao field to verify their names and issue new tickets, so that it was evenly distributed. However, there was too little porridge and too many monks, and many of the weak waited all day without getting a meal. Moreover, those in charge of cooking the porridge did not pay attention to cleanliness. The rice was only washed once before being put into the pot. The pot was buried in the ground, and mud and flies fell into the pot as it cooked. When the porridge was cooked, it looked like mung bean porridge, and the disaster victims could not swallow it. They requested that rice be issued so that they could cook it themselves. The Relief and Recovery Association did not approve this for fear of carelessness. As for the rice for the porridge, it was the 2,500 small bags (equivalent to 500 bags) donated by Xiong Shihui, and the 82 bags of rice smuggled for export that were seized by the Xunhu Rice Grain Inspection Office. Very little was purchased, and what was originally available is now almost exhausted.

The refugee shelters are currently being built actively. The one run by the Water Disaster Relief Committee can accommodate 10,000 people, and the one donated by private individuals can accommodate 1,000 people. It is expected that they will be able to start taking in refugees around the 20th of this month. It is planned to provide one porridge and one meal per day, with able-bodied men working in exchange for relief. The work-for-relief plan includes: First step (1) Leveling the base of the old city wall and filling in the nearby ditches to increase official property, and as a preparatory project for extending the Huan Cheng Road and building the Jiujiang-Hukou Highway in the future. (2) Digging up soil from the Dajiao field mountain and filling in the Lianhua Pond in the city, which is most prone to flooding, to increase official property. The second step is to repair the breaches and repair the dikes. The third step is to repair the county road between Jiujiang and Huangmei. The first step of the project has been inspected by Zhou Baipeng and Jin Shizhong, an engineer from the Junpu Bureau, who believe it is feasible. Jin Shizhong and the planner Liu Lixiu are currently preparing a budget, and construction will begin as soon as the relief funds are distributed.

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association recently remitted 20,000 yuan, which was handed over to Zhou Baipeng to handle emergency relief. This money is currently stored in the Central Branch Bank and has not been touched. Zhou is scheduled to go to the ninth and eighth districts north of the Yangtze River and the seventh district south of the Yangtze River, which have the most serious disaster situations, for a week starting on the 16th. Then, he will issue disaster victims with exchange coupons printed in half-yuan denominations, which they can take to nearby entrusted stores to exchange for cash. Distributing 20,000 yuan in relief funds among more than 150,000 disaster victims is like trying to put out a fire with a cup of water. Moreover, the northwest wind has been quite strong these days, and even wearing lined clothes does not feel warm. It is truly tragic that the disaster victims are crying out in both hunger and cold. (September 16th)

Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Transportation Temporarily Suspended

Yangzhou Correspondence: Regarding the water situation in the canal, a report from the Jiangdu section yesterday stated that the water level at the Sanggou Gate had dropped from one zhang and five chi to one zhang and four chi and eight cun, and then rose another cun, currently standing at one zhang and four chi and nine cun. However, water has still flooded into the cities near the Yangzhou East Custom House. The Shaoti dam construction project was suspended for one day on the 15th due to wind and rain. The entire city of Shaobozhen is covered with rubble, and rotting corpses are still floating in. The Shaobozhen Flood Relief Association has dispatched laborers to clean the streets and wash away the stench for the sake of transportation and hygiene. It has also determined the number of disaster victims and is distributing porridge daily. In addition, in Xinghua County, which was most severely affected by the disaster, there are still 300,000 disaster victims, including 2,000 who are gathered in the county hall awaiting relief. County Magistrate Hua is helpless and has telegraphed the Jiangsu Charity Relief Association, saying that ships will be dispatched to transport them to Yangzhou. The office here is also unable to accommodate them and has telegraphed the General Association for instructions. Transportation between Yangzhou and Zhenjiang was completely suspended on the 15th, and Shanghai newspapers have not arrived. It is said that because the people downstream are afraid of the river tide backflow and the waves eroding the dikes, a gong-beating crowd incident occurred again on the 15th. The various shipping companies have decided to temporarily open the Zhenqing-Zhenyou route (the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou short route is temporarily suspended). The Taixing-Taidong-Taiyan three-wheel route in Taixian has been opened by the Dada, Dasheng, Dayuan, and Jiangtai four companies to transport refugees, and relief passes will be sold along with the tickets. It will be implemented on the 16th.

Central Disaster Survey Committee Arrives in Bengbu

Surveying the Disaster Situation and Inspecting the Water Situation in the Lower Reaches of the Huai River

Bengbu Correspondence: This year's flood in Anhui Province has been classified as second class by the central government. Yan Zhuang, a member of the Executive Yuan's Relief Committee, and Hong Hui, a member of the Relief Committee's Disaster Survey Committee, have successively arrived in Anhui to handle disaster survey and relief matters. Zhao Jianan and Gui Fang, relief workers dispatched by Yan Zhuang, recently came to Bengbu with 50,000 yuan in relief tickets to handle emergency relief in Wuhe, Shouxian, Huoqiu, and Linhuai in northern Anhui. Hong Hui completed the disaster survey in southern Anhui and arrived in Bengbu early on the 15th with an engineer, staying at the Transportation Villa. They met with local gentry to investigate the flood situation. According to Hong, they will first investigate the disaster situation in the lower reaches of the Huai River and the causes of the disaster, and then go to the disaster areas in the counties along the Huai River to conduct separate surveys. They will conduct a detailed investigation of the Huai River situation and implement a work-for-relief method to guide the Huai River and repair the dikes in the future. At 2:00 PM today, Hong and others took the first train to Linhuai and then to Wuhe to survey the disaster situation and the Huai River water situation. (September 16th)

Shandong National Flood Emergency Relief Association Established

Jinan Correspondence: This year's flood in the Yangtze River Basin is vast, and as many as 35 counties in this province have been flooded. Millions of disaster victims are crying out for food and relief is urgently needed. Li Shuchun, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, proposed organizing the Shandong National Flood Emergency Relief Association at the 82nd provincial government meeting to provide relief, and submitted the organizational outline. After discussion, it was decided that the provincial committee, the president of the high court, and the secretary-general of the provincial government should review it, make slight amendments, and submit it to the provincial government's standing committee today. The review case was approved and the association was organized and established on the same day and began its work. The organizational outline of the association is recorded below: Article 1: This association shall be organized by two members of the provincial party department, two members of the provincial government, two members of the military agencies, two members of the provincial relief association, two members of the mass organizations, and one member of the Jinan municipal government, appointed by the provincial government. One member shall be designated as the chairman. Article 2: This association shall establish a General Affairs Office and a Relief Fundraising Office. The directors of the offices shall be elected by all members. Article 3: The General Affairs Office shall establish a Documentation Group, an Accounting Group, and a General Affairs Group. The Relief Fundraising Office shall establish a Donation and Investigation Group, a Relief Distribution Group, and a Procurement and Transportation Group. Article 4: Each group shall have one director and one deputy director, and several staff members, who shall be selected and concurrently appointed by the provincial government from among the staff of various agencies and organizations upon the request of the association. If necessary for the needs of the work, several clerks and secretaries may be employed. Article 5: All directors and staff members of this association are honorary positions, but may be given travel and accommodation expenses when necessary for the performance of their duties. The clerks and secretaries shall be given salaries by this association at its discretion. Article 6: This association may appoint enthusiastic philanthropists as members or advisors of this association to assist in the work of this association. Article 7: All members of the committee and advisors of this association are honorary positions. Article 8: The expenses of this association shall be determined by this association and submitted to the provincial government for approval by the Department of Finance, and shall not be paid from relief funds. Article 9: If there are any matters not covered in this outline, they may be submitted to the provincial government for amendment. Article 10: This outline shall be implemented from the date of approval and promulgation by the provincial government.

Strengthening Coastal Defense in Fujian

Fuzhou Correspondence: Guangxi's troops have invaded the border of Hunan, which has been reported in the newspapers. The Fujian Provincial Government also recently received reports that Guangdong has recently sent troops under Huang Renhuan and Zhang Ruigui to garrison Raoping, Dabu, Raoping, and Pingyuan in the area bordering the four counties of Zhao'an, Pinghe, Yongding, and Shanghang in Fujian Province, with the intention of entering Fujian. The government immediately telegraphed Zhang Zhen, the commander of the 49th Division of the Land Army stationed in Zhangzhou, to deploy troops to strengthen the border defense in case of emergency. Yesterday, we received a reply from Commander Zhang stating that he had followed instructions and ordered his subordinates to strictly defend and await orders. However, according to a report from an agent stationed in Chaozhou and Shantou, the Guangdong troops stationed in Chaozhou and Shantou, although claiming to be two divisions, are actually less than one division strong. They are digging trenches and holding firm, using them to defend against our army's suppression, with no intention of advancing. It is said that Chen Jitang's troops only have four divisions, most of which are in the Shaoguan area. The remaining troops are gathered in Guangzhou, ostensibly to prevent internal changes, but in reality, they have no spare capacity to invade Fujian. In order to strengthen the border defense, the provincial government ordered the division to strengthen its defenses and, given that the Guangdong-Guangxi military conflict has already broken out and the defense of southern Fujian is of great importance, appointed Fang Shengtao, the Director of the Security Department, to inspect the lower reaches and allocated 50,000 yuan for the inspection expenses. Fang is waiting for provincial committee member Lin Zhiyuan to return to the province before departing. He will first go to Xinghua, then to Quanzhou, Xiamen, and Zhangzhou, and will take about three weeks to return to the province.

About the Nakamura Incident: Chen Xingya Departs to Investigate

Speaking to Reporters, He Encourages Himself with the Word "Impartiality"

Shenyang Correspondence: Since the Nakamura Incident occurred, the friendly relations between China and Japan have suddenly become strained. The case remains unresolved, and complications have arisen. Vice Commander Zhang, to demonstrate our sincerity, has specially dispatched Northeast Gendarmerie Commander Chen to investigate the truth, hoping to establish a foundation for a peaceful resolution of this incident. Mr. Chen, accompanied by over twenty staff members, departed on the thirteenth for the Xing'an reclamation area. The following is a record of his conversation with reporters: (Question) Sir, you have been ordered to depart for an investigation, a mission of utmost importance. What steps will you take to conduct the investigation? (Answer) Sino-Japanese relations have always been harmonious. Since the negotiations over the Nakamura Incident began, they have turned bleak. International disputes depend on peaceful understanding. Investigation is the basic work to obtain a peaceful resolution. Before obtaining the true results of the investigation, I do not wish to comment on the incident itself. This time, I have been ordered to depart, and I will uphold the word "impartiality" in my actions. I will conduct a careful investigation with an objective attitude, and I will never favor one side, to show our sincerity, and hope to achieve the purpose of a peaceful resolution. (Question) What will be the future steps in the negotiations? (Answer) My mission is a purely investigative task. When I return from the investigation, it will be the end of my personal mission. The future steps in the negotiations are the task of the diplomatic authorities. (Question) What is your estimate of the future outcome of this case? (Answer) International peace depends on the coordination and understanding between nations. I have already said this before. The Chinese nation takes courtesy and peace as the foundation of its nation for thousands of years. We do not wish others to impose upon us what we do not wish to impose upon others. Sino-Japanese relations are as close as lips and teeth. If we can understand and support each other, we can maintain the permanent glory of both nations. The so-called Nakamura Incident is a small matter. After this "impartial" investigation, the clouds will clear and the sun will shine, and we will enter a smooth path towards a peaceful and satisfactory resolution.

Anhui Provincial Government Officially Handles Special Tax

Wuhu Correspondence: Regarding the issue of opium prohibition in Anhui Province, since the Central Opium Prohibition Committee established opium suppression and investigation offices in Bengbu, Wuhu, Datong, and Anqing, and appointed Hao Zihua as the director, the people of Anhui believed it was a disguised form of opium public sale, and protested vehemently. Later, the Opium Prohibition Committee and the Executive Yuan simultaneously issued orders to abolish the offices. The Anhui Provincial Government also followed the order, instructing all counties to supervise and abolish them by a deadline. At that time, the establishment of suppression and investigation sub-offices in various townships and towns, which the suppression and investigation office had planned to establish, was also suddenly suspended. Although the Central Government issued a clear order to abolish the suppression and investigation office, Hao Zihua has been running around between the province and Bengbu, with a very active attitude. The suppression and investigation head office and the Wuhu branch office are also proceeding as before. The work of suppression and tax collection is becoming more intense, all under the direction of Section Chief Kong Qizhong. Whether the tax money is still reported to the Central Government or directly sent to Anqing is unknown. At the same time, rumors of renaming and reorganizing the suppression and investigation office are also widespread. Indeed, the provincial government's 214th meeting last week put forward the discussion. Because it had already obtained the approval of Commander-in-Chief Chiang, it formally passed the establishment of a special tax office in Anhui Province, and still appointed Hao Zihua as the director. The reason why the provincial government must handle the special tax may also be caused by the environment. According to the propaganda from the special tax office, this year's flood in Anhui Province is unusually heavy. The people are miserable and in dire need of relief. Opium prohibition should be strictly enforced, and disaster relief is especially urgent. The method of prohibition emphasizes clearing up. Investigating the private planting households in this province is a violation of the law. However, in this autumn of severe disaster, after the harvest, if no change is made, not only will drugs accumulate, causing endless troubles, but the people's only hope for survival will be plunged into desperation. Now, in order to be lenient to the past and strictly prohibit the future, so that drugs can be suppressed and the disaster-stricken people can be relieved, we have referred to the successful cases in Henan and Hubei and handled the special tax. After this case was passed, Hao immediately telegraphed Section Chief Kong Qizhong to go to the province from Wuhu to formulate regulations and actively prepare. The head office will still be located in Wuhu. However, due to the floodwaters not receding, it is inconvenient to handle matters, so it is planned to temporarily set up in Bengbu. However, Wuhu is close to the Yangtze River and is the main hub for the import and export of special goods, so it has been decided to set up a branch office first. Now, the office has drafted a notice explaining the reasons for the establishment and notifying the people of Anhui, and ordering special merchants and planting and smoking households to abide by the regulations and not to seek impunity. News of the 7th Regiment: A comrade has arrived from this regiment via Guangdong and has not yet received a detailed report. However, we know that the 7th Regiment had 5,000 men and 3,000 guns in September 1930 (the 19th year of the Republic of China). It decided to unite with Zhu and Mao, so it once went from Guangxi to the southwest of Hunan Province, and soon returned to Guizhou from southern Hunan, heading east to northern Guangdong. When this comrade left the regiment, its headquarters was in southwestern Jiangxi Province. The roads they have traveled before and after are more than 2,000 miles. On the way, they did not do any work among the workers and peasants. Their only task and purpose was to join Zhu De and Mao Zedong. The regiment fought many times with the enemy and was defeated each time. Now, only 1,000 men and 700 guns remain.

(46) Talks with Xiang (Zhongfa) and Gorupin on April 7

Xiang (the following is his talk): A comrade from the Central Committee in charge of internal liaison was arrested on April 5 (Sunday). The location was inside a trade union building. When he was arrested, he was found to have a letter from the comrades in Liaoning Prison to the Red Relief Society, a letter from the Provincial Committee (the content is unknown), a letter from the Central Committee to the National Labor Union, 1,000 yuan in foreign currency, and an address of the Anhui Provincial Committee. One receipt for the comrades of the Central Committee groups. After he was arrested, the police were on constant guard there, so soon another seven comrades were captured. Among these seven people, one was the Liaison Director of the National Labor Union Action Team, one was the Liaison Officer of the Red Relief Society, one was the Instructor of the Unemployed Workers, and the others were the Personal Liaison Officers of the Central Committee (including one woman). The arrest of the first person was caused by taking risks. (Asdre asked what he meant by taking risks, but Xiang only replied that according to a certain report). Xiang continued that this arrested comrade had been working in the Central Committee for a long time, so he was deeply trusted. In 1927, he was Xiang's private secretary, so he was very familiar with the addresses of the thirty-one people currently responsible for important work in various places (including twenty-two people working in the various groups of the Central Committee, three in the Provincial Committee, four in the Trade Union, and two in the Red Relief Society). Since they were familiar with our addresses, we had to move immediately and inform the Technical Department of the Provincial Committee to find a new house. Xiang also said that in order to implement this plan quickly, he had convened a meeting in a certain hotel. The number of attendees included the Liaison Director of each district, the Personal Liaison Officer of the Provincial Committee, the Liaison Director of Shanghai, and a certain Technical Secretary of the Provincial Committee. In order to avoid attracting the attention of others, they had to shout loudly during the discussion, but unfortunately, this caused the intervention of the watchman and summoned the police.

Asdre: Why are you so panicked when only a few people are arrested? Are you recklessly appointing untrustworthy comrades to this important work, which leads to not being able to trust them?

Xiang: Because the first arrested comrade knows our situation very well, and he is very weak, so we have to be cautious.

Asdre: Have you not heard that the liaison work of the Central Committee does not need to be done like this? Why are there so many Liaison Directors? How many are there now? Why do the comrades in the Central Committee have to draw receipts for their living expenses? What are these receipts for? In my opinion, these Liaison Directors should be cancelled immediately, and they should not be given any other titles. Because once there is a director, there must be several secretaries under the director. Following this, will we not increase a huge amount of expenses? The Party's money must be distributed according to the overall needs. It is really impossible to favor any aspect, including the comrades employed by the Central Committee. We have mentioned this to you many times, but I did not expect that it is still the same today. Moreover, if the number of people is small, on the one hand, it can save money, and on the other hand, it can avoid danger.

Xiang: We have also tried our best to reduce the staff in various places, but so far it has been ineffective. This kind of problem is very easy to talk about, but very difficult to implement. Moreover, in such an environment, if there are not so many people, how can the responsibility of liaison be carried out, will it not be more restrictive?

Asdre: You may hand this matter over to the Bureau for handling, and then refer to our plan. You can try to reduce the existing 150 people by at least half. The principle is that every comrade can be effective and can get an accurate distribution in work.

Xiang: Feng (Yuxiang) recently sent two representatives to contact us. One of them used to be our comrade. It is not clear what the purpose of his contact with us is. Moskin had a conversation today with someone who used to be one of our comrades. It is only known that Feng has now realized his past mistakes and is eager for us to provide assistance. Moreover, Feng plans to go to Berlin via Siberia in the future. Pang, the former commander of the 2nd Division of the National Army (now in Shanghai), and Tan's troops also have a tendency to contact us. This issue requires the instructions of the Congress.

Asdre: You can immediately report the results of Moskin's conversation with the representative and the purposes of the other people mentioned above, so that we can have a basis. What I want to mention to you today is the letter we wrote to you last time, because the enemy is now working hard to eliminate and divide the internal Red Army. We should pay very close attention to this point. It is too strange that three representatives of the enemy are contacting us at the same time. We should be cautious in all aspects and not easily sign contracts with them or agree to any conditions. At most, we can only use them. We must remember that they are our enemies, not our friends. Or even because some of our comrades are currently working in their troops, they are eager to fool us. We will consider it in detail when your report is submitted.

Xiang: We have recently received a report saying that some comrades are currently contacting the officers under Yue Weijun (Yue himself was previously intercepted by us on the Ping-Han Road). The person in charge of the contact is Peng, an officer of that department. They are willing to redeem Yue for 100,000 yuan.

Asdre: You can immediately notify the comrades of the 1st Army Corps and tell them to act cautiously. The most important point is to strictly imprison Yue and not let him escape. Also, tell them not to kill this person, because killing him is useless. We must keep him as a guarantee.

Xiang: We recently sent Comrade Tong Mingxuan (transliteration) to Henan to serve as secretary. He was originally a textile worker in Shanghai. He was arrested for something and tasted the iron window for a year. He has just been released from prison. He is indeed a very good comrade.

Asdre: What kind of work did he do before he was arrested? When exactly was he released from prison? Has he fully recovered to his original state now? Politically speaking, does he have a firm spirit?

Xiang and Ge: Before he was arrested, he was the secretary of a certain group. He was released on New Year's Day this year. He still worked as usual after his release and completed a short-term training in the Party.

Asdre: It is best to give him some time to rest before he goes to Henan. His expenses will of course be provided by the Red Relief Society. In short, we must first help comrades recover their health, and then provide them with daily necessities before we can get practical results.

Recent reports on various strikes

The recent strike of 24 silk factories was launched at the same time. At that time, we only had contact with four factories and seven female workers. The youth comrades only had contact with two female workers. In a certain silk factory, there are twelve female workers who are very close to each other. Now we are trying to get close to them. In addition, we also have a public female workers' school. As for the aforementioned seven people, four of them are our comrades, but they are very timid. Most of the work and guidance given to them by the district committee cannot be carried out. Even when meetings are held, they do not attend. The Party originally promised to give them one yuan for each meeting they attended, but now it has stopped paying them, so they have refused to attend. During the strike, we did not do any work. Although this strike was launched at the same time, it was very short-lived. At most, it was only three days before work was resumed. The Kuomintang forced a silk factory to resume work during this strike. The silk factories that resumed work were resumed voluntarily by the workers. Therefore, their goals were completely unachieved. Only one silk factory with 800 workers agreed to increase the wages by 50%. We anticipate that this kind of strike will be repeated soon, so we are now preparing everything. (To be continued)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

A Robbery and Kidnapping Occurs in Dazhangjing: Last night (16th) at 9:30 PM, the house of farmer Han Lisheng in Tu Ji Village, No. 7 Tu, Dazhangjing, a southwestern suburb of the city, was suddenly visited by seven or eight bandits carrying a pistol, iron bars, and daggers, etc., forcing the victim to tell them where the silver was hidden. Han said that he was poor and had no money. They then pried open the wooden box and searched it. They only found one hundred copper coins and nothing else of value. The bandits were angry and kidnapped his seven-year-old son, heading towards the southwest Pudong bank. The victim was hit in the waist with an iron bar and stabbed in the little finger. He immediately reported it to the City Second Police Station, which sent police to investigate, but returned without success. Today, the First District Office reported the situation to the County Government, requesting that it be ordered to rescue the child.

Letter Announcing the Start of Emergency Repair of the Sea Dike: Xue Xingbei, the director of the Jiangnan Water Conservancy and Sea Dike Engineering Office, along with Standing Committee Member Sun, County Magistrate Shen, Bureau Chief Sun, Regiment Commander Cao, and various gentry, inspected the sea dike at Jinshanwei on the 13th. Technical staff member Shen Baozhang was left there to oversee the project. He himself went to the province to report the situation to the Water Conservancy Bureau, which approved an allocation of 10,000 yuan to purchase materials such as wood and stones and transport them to the work site for emergency repair. Work officially started yesterday. Director Xue recently sent a quick letter to Chairman Cai of the Chamber of Commerce, saying that with the 20,000 yuan already received, emergency repair work is underway to reassure everyone. However, the tide has been high in recent days, and the water level in the low-lying streets and along the rivers in the city is almost level with the banks. If the weather is clear before the 18th day of the lunar calendar this month, danger can be avoided.

Changshu

Request to Transfer Jurisdiction in the Case of Public Security Personnel Being Accused: Xiao Gensheng, who lives in Junziju Alley outside the South Gate, was detained by the Public Security Bureau for selling opium. Xiao Gensheng's mother and son were sentenced to imprisonment and fined over 200 yuan. At that time, Xiao wanted to pay Director Lu Zhibin of the Public Security Bureau and various section members and clerks a bribe, with receipts as evidence, in order to avoid being punished. Unexpectedly, the judge still imposed a fine. Xiao then revealed the matter of the Public Security Bureau's personnel accepting bribes in court. Then, the county government considered it necessary to thoroughly investigate this case and conducted a preliminary investigation. The trial was scheduled to open on the 19th of this month. The accused, such as Section Chief Lu, because of their close relationship with County Magistrate Tan, who also handles judicial affairs, submitted a petition to the county government, stating that the case had been petitioned to the High Court for transfer of jurisdiction and requesting that the files be sent. Yesterday, it was heard that the county government had approved it, and the case files could be submitted on the 17th.

Three Canals in Henan Section, Jointly Dredged with Nantong County: The southern end of the Three Canals in Henan Section of Shazhou City was blocked by port dams built by farmers in the Fourth District. The authorities have repeatedly advised and explained the conditions. The farmers in the Fourth District began to remove it, and the work has already started on the 14th and was completed yesterday. However, the conditions discussed by the Fourth and Fifth Districts this time are that the Fourth District (one of the districts removing the dam) should propose to the Fifth District that the downstream of the Thirteen Weir Port Three Canals in Nantong be jointly dredged by the Fourth and Fifth Districts. Now that the Fifth District has recognized this condition, the people of the Fifth District agreed to open the dam, otherwise they would rather die than comply. As for the downstream of the Thirteen Weir Port Three Canals to be dredged this time, it belongs to the southern border, and its route is about eight or nine li. Nantong County has already negotiated properly.

Nantong

Coastal Defense Against Sea Bandits: In the sea areas of Tong, Ru, and Hai counties in northern Jiangsu, it is now the season for fishermen to catch jellyfish, and sea bandits have come again. There are as many as ten bandit ships drifting in the sea, with more than 300 bandits. They invaded Dayu Town, burned and looted, kidnapped people, and injured police and militia. The counties have now sent police teams to defend against them. Knowing that there is preparation, the bandits retreated northward in large numbers. There are still five bandit ships anchored in Juegang.

Methods for Soliciting Clothing and Bedding for Disaster Victims: Tongyi has set up a total of ten shelters to accommodate disaster victims from various counties along the Grand Canal in northern Jiangsu, with a total of more than 3,000 men and women. The disaster victims are all thinly clothed, and some are even unable to cover their bodies. Various groups and organizations are launching donations to prepare clothing and bedding. On the one hand, primary and secondary school students throughout the county are soliciting donations widely. The county government, considering the custom of Haimen, a neighboring county, where dowries are often given when daughters are married, and many families often have a lot of accumulated cotton quilts, specially sent a letter to County Magistrate Zhang of Haimen, asking him to send personnel to households to solicit old quilts and send them to Tong to be given to the disaster victims.

The Issue of Increasing the Surcharge on Salt Fields: Nantong's fields have always been divided into people's fields and salt fields. The tax rate on salt fields is very light. This year, the local funds are insufficient and there is no way to open up new sources of income. After deliberation by the Finance Rectification Committee, it was decided to increase the local surcharge on salt fields by two yuan. The county government submitted a report to the Provincial Transport Office for approval. The Transport Office has ordered the various salt fields in the Yuzhao area to immediately convene the salt farmers to discuss and reply.

Wuxi

A Bizarre Homicide Occurred on Dongxin Road. Hua Guisheng, a Jiangbei native residing at No. 7, Dongxin Road, outside Guangfu Gate, opposite the Liao Sheng Theater, was 50 years old. He cohabitated with a woman surnamed Xie and ran the Hua Jing Ji Stone Company, possessing some savings. In recent years, the relationship between the cohabitating couple had been strained, leading to frequent arguments. On the 16th, another dispute erupted, with both sides exchanging taunts and refusing to yield. The argument escalated into a physical altercation. It is unknown how, but Hua's kidney area was injured. He immediately turned pale, collapsed to the ground, and his breath became faint, on the verge of death. Xie, realizing the gravity of the situation, immediately hired someone to fetch Dr. Zhu Chaoliang from Tongren Hospital to treat him. However, Hua had already died and could not be saved. Afterward, the local Second Precinct received the news and dispatched police officers to investigate, but they could not ascertain the truth. The circumstances of Hua's death are quite bizarre. After the incident, Hua's cohabitating partner, Xie, attempted to flee to Changzhou. Fortunately, the deceased's family intercepted her at the train station. Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, they prepared a coffin and hastily prepared Gui Sheng's body for burial.

Court Autopsy of Female Worker Injured by Scalding. Hongyun, the daughter-in-law of Liu Si, a guest resident of Futian Lane in the city, worked as a silk factory basin worker outside Guangfu Gate along the city wall. On the 26th of last month, she was scalded by hot water by a fellow worker, Qin Shenshi, leaving scars. Liu Si negotiated with Qin and arranged for medical treatment. Unexpectedly, Hongyun died on the 16th of this month in the afternoon. Yesterday, the ward leader Wu Shuntai, along with Liu Si, reported to the county court's prosecutor's office at 3:30 PM, requesting that someone be sent for an autopsy. The autopsy revealed that she had died of illness following the burn sustained during her life, and her family was instructed to prepare the body for burial. Qin Shenshi was taken into custody pending review.

Letter Requesting the Return of Borrowed Launches. The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce received letters from the Taihu Lianghe Company's Wuxi Branch and the Ruishengxiang Steamboat Bureau, stating that they were ordered to dispatch six launches, including the Xinyufufu, Feihuang, Xinqingrui, Xinzhenxing, Nanlong, and Xieyu, to Zhenjiang to transport and rescue refugees. They complied and set sail to Zhenjiang on the 29th of last month and the 2nd of this month, respectively. It has been over half a month, and they have not been returned. Now, the water level in Wuxi is low, and transportation can be restored. However, there are no launches available to operate. They are at a loss and requested their return. After receiving the letters, the Chamber of Commerce sent an official letter to the county government yesterday, requesting that the aforementioned launches be identified and returned.

Appeal from Brewers Regarding Compulsory Tax Payment. The Wuxi tobacco license tax was contracted to Dou Luyi for collection this autumn. He rigorously reorganized the brewers in the rural areas and established a branch office in Xinan Huadafang Village in the southern countryside. He ordered the peasant households to register and pay taxes according to regulations, and those who violated the regulations would be summoned and punished. Currently, 94 peasant households, including Mo Yongsen, from the town, jointly submitted reports to the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau and the county government, stating that the rural households in remote areas have no capital or licenses. They only brew alcohol during farming slack periods using agricultural products, using the dregs to feed pigs and livestock, and the manure to fertilize the fields to increase production. This is different from large-scale wholesalers and retailers. This type of sideline business for farmers, although small, has the basis for improvement and should be encouraged. Moreover, since the implementation of tobacco and alcohol licenses, it has been more than 20 years, and there has never been an order to collect taxes from these rural households. Even in Jiangbei Taixing, Wuxian Hengjingdu Village, and other places where more alcohol is produced, there has never been an order to rural households to pay taxes and obtain licenses. This year's flood was particularly severe, and Xinan, bordering Taihu Lake, was severely affected. Most of the farmers are already destitute. If taxes are levied indiscriminately, the farmers will not be able to bear it. They request that measures be taken to stop this and save the impoverished people whose livelihoods are on the verge of collapse.

Suzhou and Changzhou Counties No Longer Accommodating Refugees. The Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs stated that the Jiangbei disaster areas are vast, and refugees are flocking in large numbers. They planned to arrange for Suzhou and Changzhou counties to accommodate them. The Wuxi Party and government agencies stated that the county is actively raising donations to provide disaster relief. If a large number of refugees were transported to Wuxi, there would be no suitable accommodation places, and the local people would be disturbed, which would hinder disaster relief efforts. Therefore, Hua Yisan, the chairman of the disaster relief committee, Li Tiping, the executive member of the county party department, and Qian Sunqing, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, went to the provincial capital together with County Magistrate Chen to separately meet with Chairman Ye of the provincial government and Director Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs. They explained the truth and requested that they be exempted from sending refugees to Wuxi. They were informed that they had just returned to the province from inspecting Jiangbei and knew that the true refugees would find it difficult to resume their businesses in the future and would not easily leave their hometowns. It had been decided to change the plan and temporarily abandon it. Yesterday, the county government also received a telegram from the province stating that Jiangbei refugees had been divided and telegraphed to Huai'an, Huaiyin, and Taixing counties to prepare accommodation centers by a certain date to accommodate them in different ways. The previous proposal to add accommodation centers in Danyang, Wujin, Wuxi, and Wuxian counties should be investigated and canceled by telegram. The county disaster relief committee has telegraphed to the fellow-townsmen associations in Beijing and Shanghai, as well as the Suzhou Wujin Chamber of Commerce, to inform them.

Danyang

Village Robbery and Assault. More than a dozen bandits armed with guns broke into the home of Zhao Shengtong, a farmer in Zhao Xiangli Village in the southern countryside, at about ten o'clock last night. They first restrained Zhao Shengtong, tied him up with ropes, and burned him with fire to force him to hand over cash. The remaining bandits dispersed to search and rob before fleeing with a roar. The case has been reported to the police for investigation.

Zhenjiang

Suining Representatives Plead for Troops and Relief. In Suining, local bandits have been rampant recently, abducting more than a hundred teachers and students in the county. The floods are also extremely severe, and the people are suffering greatly. In addition to sending telegrams to the province to request rescue, local agencies and organizations also sent Zhu Bohong as a representative to the province yesterday to petition for help. After arriving in the province, Zhu visited Chairman Ye of the provincial government, Director Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs, Director Li of the Security Department, and Hu Jianchun, the director of the Jiangbei Temporary Disaster Relief Association, to plead for troops and relief. According to the results of their petition, regarding the banditry, the Department of Civil Affairs and the Security Department have already telegraphed the Jiangsu Pacification Superintendent to dispatch troops to suppress them. Regarding the local armed forces, Director Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs promised to change the County Public Security Bureau into a section and allocate a portion of the funds to expand the county police force. Regarding disaster relief, Director Hu and Director Hu promised to pay special attention, and Director Hu also approved an order to the county to ban brewing alcohol to save grain for the people's food.

Departmental Committee Orders Telegram Survey of the Situation on the Eastern Embankment. The Provincial Department of Civil Affairs previously received telegrams from Suzhou, Songjiang, Changzhou, and Zhenjiang counties, stating that the people of Gaochun County were about to release water from the Eastern Dam. Because it had a great impact on the counties south of the Yangtze River, they specially commissioned Jiang Fuqin to go to the county for investigation. Yesterday, Jiang telegraphed from Chun to report on the situation of the embankment, saying that he had gone to the Eastern Dam for inspection with local officials and gentry and saw that the foundation of the dam was intact, the water was four inches over the dam, and the people of Wan had no intention of opening the dam. However, the disaster situation was extremely severe and needed urgent relief.

Yangzhou

Accident Involving Shunli Kerosene Boat Results in Eight Deaths. The Shanghai Meida Kerosene Company recently entrusted the Qiaji Sailing Ship Company to transport 1,000 pairs of oil barrels, worth about 20,000 yuan, to the Shaobo branch for sale in the Shunli sailboat. When it sailed to Erdaoqiao in this territory, it could not move upstream due to the rapid flow of the canal and was anchored there for about two weeks. A few days ago, it was suddenly hit by a strong wind, which broke the mast of the boat. In addition, the rapid current of the water caused the entire hull to be shattered. The goods drifted with the waves. It is said that there were eight crew members on the boat, all of whom were killed. Their bodies drifted away without a trace. The Qiaji Sailing Ship Company, after hearing the news, has sent Zhang Jingshui to Yangzhou to investigate the truth of the accident and has also sent people to recover the bodies.

Live Burial Case Occurs in Baimamiao. Tong Lixiang, a farmer in Baimamiao in the fourth district of this county, had a quarrel with his clansmen Tong Xinquan, Tong Xinkun, and Tong Xinyou on the ninth of this month. He was tied up with ropes by Xinquan and others, beaten, and then buried alive in a nearby rice field. Later, the deceased's son found out about it and reported it to the police for investigation. It is now known that the prosecutor's office of the court dispatched Prosecutor Ju and autopsy officials to the scene of the incident yesterday to dig out the body of Tong Lixiang. He was still tied with ropes, and the autopsy confirmed that there were injuries.

Jiaxing

Finance Bureau Requests Extension of Land Tax Surcharge. Xu Maojian, director of the Jiaxing County Finance Bureau, stated that He County had suffered continuous floods, and many crops had been submerged. The farmers were struggling to raise funds for rescue and could barely cope. The deadline for the land tax surcharge was approaching. Director Xu telegraphed the Department of Finance yesterday, requesting that the surcharge be extended. He also instructed the officials of Jia and Xiu to inform the tax collectors to continue collecting the tax at the original rate of 4 yuan, 1 jiao, 6 fen, and 4 li before receiving provincial orders.

Removal of the Director of the Xinfeng Chamber of Commerce Branch. The Jiaxing County Chamber of Commerce previously appointed Feng Tongzhai as the director of the Xinfeng branch office. However, the merchants in the area jointly opposed it and requested the revocation of the appointment. The Chamber of Commerce ignored this, which led to a worsening relationship between Feng and the merchants in the town. Later, Feng was also elected as a standing committee member of the meat industry and contracted to collect slaughter surcharges. He even asked for hundreds of yuan from his colleagues in the name of fees. Members collected evidence and filed a complaint with the judiciary. The court summoned him several times for interrogation and ordered him to pay a bail bond and await summons. On the 16th, several representatives of the meat industry requested the County Chamber of Commerce to order Feng to hand over the affairs of the association. At the same time, the Xinfeng merchants submitted a request to replace the director of the branch office. The County Chamber of Commerce stated that, according to the Trade Union Law, it currently had no authority to order him to hand over the affairs of the association and would review the matter after the judicial department resolved it. The Chamber of Commerce decided yesterday to approve the request of the Xinfeng merchants for a replacement and set the 22nd to convene a meeting of the members of the branch office in the Xinfeng Town Office to elect three candidates to report to the Chamber for approval.

Hangzhou

Accident Caused by Overloaded Tugboat on the Qiantang River. Wang Zemin, the commissioner of the Jiangxi Eastern Party and Government Committee of the Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, came to Hangzhou from Jiangxi at the beginning of this month to meet with Chairman Zhang of the provincial government to discuss refugee and border defense issues between the two provinces. Later, due to the departure of the troops, he rushed back to Jiangxi Eastern and chartered a private boat owned by Mao Mingquan. Yang Yongnian from Guo Zaihang acted as an agent. Unexpectedly, the boat owner and the agent colluded and secretly loaded heavy objects. When they reached the Mengjia Yan area, they were hit by waves and the entire boat capsized. Wang and his ten entourages fell into the water. Fortunately, they were rescued by the Tiana Wheel. Very few official documents and belongings were saved. Wang has sent a letter to the provincial government, ordering the Department of Construction to severely punish the Guo Zaihang and others to avoid danger to passengers.

Ningbo

Theft Case in Shenjia Shetou. Du Chuchao, a resident of Shenjia Shetou, Xia'an Village, Yisi Township, Yuyao, made a living by farming and had some savings. At about ten o'clock last night, as he was about to go to bed, more than a dozen bandits suddenly broke into his house, holding pistols, and ransacked the house for about an hour. It is estimated that they stole more than 200 yuan in cash and many pieces of clothing and miscellaneous items.

Jiangbei Shore Water Police. The Jin Changxiang sesame oil shop, located at the corner of Yangshan Dian Lane next to the Xiaocai Market on the Jiangbei shore of Ningbo, accidentally started a fire while frying sesame seeds at about one o'clock this morning. The fire spread to the neighboring Yongdexing paper store, Dehe cigarette paper store, and more than a dozen households, including Li Yaoting's residence. The fire was extinguished after more than three hours. It was found that the destroyed houses were all owned by the Li family, and all the affected households had fire insurance.

Shangyu

Attempting to Dissuade Husband from Arguing, Suffered Humiliation and Committed Suicide. Zhang Guixiang, a farmer in Zhuling Bridge, West Township, quarreled with his neighbor, Xiao Liansheng, over the latter's failure to return several liters of rice borrowed during a heavy rainstorm on the 20th of last month. Zhang Guixiang's wife, Liang Meiying, went to mediate after hearing about the quarrel. Unexpectedly, Zhang Guixiang turned his anger on his wife and tried to assault her. Liang Meiying, seeing the situation was not good, fled into Xiao Liansheng's house. Zhang Guixiang, in a fit of rage, followed her in. Liang Meiying, in a state of desperation, turned around and struck him with a stool. At that moment, her aunt, who had just received news from a Buddhist nun's house, rushed over and saw her daughter-in-law hitting her husband with a stool. Thinking she was a shrew, she entered Xiao Liansheng's house and tried to drag her back to punish her according to family law. Liang Meiying, seeing the situation, rushed out and ran away. Her mother and son followed behind her. Unexpectedly, in a split second, Liang Meiying disappeared. Zhang Guixiang's mother and son initially suspected that she had fled into Zhang Xiaogou's house next to the road and even asked Xiaogou to hand her over. Shortly after, a crab-catching shepherd boy from the village reported that Liang Meiying's body had been found in a nearby river. They then realized that she had committed suicide by drowning. The mother and son were filled with remorse.

Chen A'gen, a Person Involved in the Case, Arrested. Ying Fengwu, the former director of the Wufu Public Security Bureau, had a misunderstanding with the local people on the night of June 7 while they were arresting Patrol Officer Sun Shengwu and policemen Wang Fenglin and Zhang Jun for gambling, which led to a conflict. Ying fled out of the side door of the bureau and somehow drowned in a nearby river. Subsequently, the county government arrested and imprisoned nine people who were the ringleaders in catching the gamblers, including Yin A'yuan, Zhou Siyi, Li A'xian, Fan A'tong, Jia Duanfu, Zhu Guobiao, and Fan Guozhen. However, Chuan Liu Jiu and Chen A'gen, an officer from the bureau, were still at large. The case had been investigated several times, but a verdict had not been reached. It is now known that Chen secretly returned to the town a few days ago and was discovered by the police officers of the Public Security Bureau, who arrested him and sent him to the county.

Taizhou

Representatives Go to the County to Petition. The additional fee on the Haimen steamship in Linhai, which the provincial government decided to use a quarter of it as an additional educational fee for the county, has been outstanding for nine months. The steamship company has refused to pay and has repeatedly been ordered by the county government to pursue payment, but without any substantial results. Therefore, the County Party Department and various legal organizations and schools in the county sent more than 20 representatives to the county government at 9:00 AM today (the 15th), requesting that the person in charge of the Haimen steamship company be detained and forced to pay. County Magistrate Xu Shixian received them and approved their request. The representatives then left.

Theft Occurs in Datian Town. More than a dozen bandits broke into the Yuanmao Nanhua store in Zhongjie, Datian Town, East Township, Linhai, last night and stole silver, cash, clothing, and other items worth more than 1,000 yuan, and also kidnapped a six-year-old child.

Shanghai City Games Day Six

Wuben Wins Women's Volleyball Championship, National Arts Competition Concludes

Today's Men's and Women's Basketball Finals, Baseball and Tennis Continued

Basketball Finals Frenzy

Men's and Women's Basketball Finals Tonight

Complimentary Tickets Invalid, Tickets One Yuan

The大会 various championships have reached the short soldier's meeting stage. Yesterday's women's volleyball finals, in the athletics field, onlookers reached thousands of people, cheering and screaming.

Wuben won the championship with excellent performance, winning over Haixing. Basketball is also white-hot, the evening basketball hall announced that it was full, and those who arrived later ate behind closed doors, there were many. Tonight's men's and women's basketball finals, it is bound to be more crowded. In order to maintain order, tickets will be sold for one silver dollar tonight. Complimentary tickets, long tickets, athlete certificates, all are invalid. The quick-footed win first. The martial arts has come to a result, the men's and women's tennis and football finals tomorrow, the conference will also announce the closing.

Women's Volleyball Finals - Wuben Wins Championship

3-1 Victory over Haixing

Haixing's Skills Also Very Good

There are two teams with great reputation in the Shanghai women's volleyball world: Wuben and Minli. Since the decline of Minli, Haixing has risen, so Wuben and Haixing stand side by side in Shanghai. In the Shanghai Women's Volleyball Tournament, the above two teams fought fiercely for the championship. As expected, they met in the finals yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. With the sound of the drums, Wuben's ambition filled the sky, and they defeated their opponents with a score of three to one, winning the women's volleyball championship. This is a great story in the history of Shanghai sports.

(1) Zhang Junwei Assembled Troops

With a Call to Arms, the Warriors Were Inspired

Wuben's success or failure depended on this battle. The honor was tied not only to the team but to the entire school. However, every ball game is driven by vigor. Without raising the military's prestige, how can victory be expected? Even if one cannot take up arms and charge forward, one should shout and cheer to help, fulfilling one's duty. Unanimously, they assembled in groups on the east corner of the field, four to five hundred people, forming a towering human mountain. With a call to arms, the sound shook the fields. The warriors' morale was high, and the momentum was strong. They struggled from defeat, initially forming a balanced situation, and then continued their efforts, finally achieving success. The result of the warriors' efforts was also due to the encouragement of their companions.

(2) Wuben Team's Talents Are Average

The Whole Team Is United, Advancing and Retreating in an Orderly Manner

Wuben's victory over Haixing was not easy. The three players in the first row, Wang, Zhang, and Li, were agile in their shots, especially Zhang Biru, who was excellent at blocking. Xue Zhijie in the second row was the soul of the team. Her skills in setting, passing, and spiking were all superb, like Jiang Taigong being here, with no taboos. It is a pity that the old wound on her finger had not healed, otherwise, she might have achieved even better results. Qian Shuyi on her left was a powerful setter who scored many points. On the right was Zhu Shangfu, who was relatively softer, but the final success came from her hands, making her a lucky general. The third row was excellent at saving balls, and saving a ball is equal to serving a ball, all of which can be relied upon to score points and win. Wang Jinfeng was good at returning blocks and escaping from danger. The left and right assistants were also capable. The talents of the whole team were average, and they cooperated well. As for the clever strategy and orderly advance and retreat, it was due to the guidance of Li Feiyun. The full team list is as follows:

First Row Second Row Third Row

Wang Xuehua Zhu Shangfu Xiao Jieying

Zhang Biru Xue Zhijie Wang Jinfeng

Li Bo Qian Shuyi Lu Meiyun

(3) Haixing Team Unlucky

Each Individual Was Excellent, But Lacked Cooperation

The Haixing team brought together the essence of various schools. Each individual talent was outstanding, and everyone praised them. However, they had not been formed for long, and lacked cooperation. In the third and fourth sets, they were unlucky and failed. The performances of Wang Nengchun in the first row and Guan Liuzhu, Situ Wei, and Huang Xingfen in the second row were praised by the audience. Separately, the first row was excellent at returning blocks, the second row was powerful in spiking, and the third row was unable to save the situation. The whole team was scattered or gathered, and leaks were frequently seen. The reason for the failure was partly due to this. Coach Li Xinbiao repeatedly gave opportunities, but it was difficult to turn the tide. The full team list is as follows:

Wuben Team That Won the Women's Volleyball Championship (Photographed by This Newspaper)

(4) With a Great Reputation, Capturing Passes and Breaking Forts

Haixing's First Win Was Very Easy

At the beginning of the match, Wuben served the ball, and Hong Ruochun struck back with a backhand, hitting the key point and winning a point. Hou Yufen added twelve points, and Haixing took the lead with 3-0, with great momentum. It became 6-2, and shortly after 11-6 to change sides. Wuben, intimidated by the enemy's reputation, appeared flustered, full of thorns, and struggling to move forward. Haixing was invincible and won every battle. Wang Ruochun and Situ Wei made the greatest contributions. The front and back three rows were neat and impressive. Their victory over the enemy was very easy. As a result, Haixing won the first set 21-14. At the beginning of the second set, Wuben still did not gain momentum until Qian Shuyi served, starting from a tie of 5-5, and rising steadily. The credit goes to the first row's infinite changes. After 11-6, Wuben's momentum was even stronger. Xue Zhijie led the whole team, striving to be active, and soon won the second set 21-16.

(5) United Efforts to Overcome the Enemy

Turning Defeat into Victory, Wuben Succeeded

The third and fourth sets were extremely tense. Haixing relied on individual skills to seek development, while Wuben used cooperative efforts to deal with them. At the beginning of the set, Haixing took the lead with 4-1. Wuben followed, and after a tie of 9-9, there was another score of 13. Haixing took the lead each time, while Wuben followed closely. Finally, thanks to the strength of Wuben's third row, they won the third set again with 21-19. In the fourth set, the two teams were evenly matched at first. Later, Haixing made progress, once leading with 11-9 and 17-13. But Wuben's cooperation suddenly showed great connection, turning danger into safety, and finally won with 21-19. The referee was Tan Tianpei.

Men's Basketball Semi-Final Results - Chih Chih and Shanghai University Win Championship

People Crazy, Chih Chih Beats Qingguang

Atmosphere Hot, Shanghai University Wins Jinan

The results of the basketball semi-finals of the four major giants were that Chih Chih and Shanghai University won the finals. Thousands of viewers, the atmosphere was frenzied. The battle between Chih Chih and Qingguang, the strength was equal. Chih Chih only surpassed in the second half, and its performance was fast and wonderful, which is commendable, especially Kong Guangyi, the main pillar of the whole team. As for Shanghai University's victory over Jinan, the situation was different, the difference was far, and the interest was also reduced.
