Township Heads in the Second District of the County Oppose Re-Evaluation of Land Prices

Peng Zhaotang Prepares a Document to Present to the County

The Shanghai County Government recently found no funds for construction and party affairs, and planned to collect them from the field. The land price in the county was previously assessed at 100 yuan per mu. The current busy Cao and various other levies are already enough for 1%, and no more can be added. Therefore, a meeting was convened to re-evaluate the land price, which was set at 115 yuan per mu. The township heads in the second district of the county believed that land prices should not be increased at this time, so they proposed at the district affairs meeting that the original price should be maintained and requested that the district office forward it to the government. It is now heard that Peng Zhaotang, the head of the district, has prepared a document to present to the county to plead for the people.

Chu Minyi's Thoughts on Investigating the Northwest

Developing the Borderlands Focuses on Transportation

The Sino-French Northwest Inspection Team traveled to the Northwest for several months. Although there were no new scientific research data, there were indeed good thoughts on developing industries in the Northwest borderlands. According to Dr. Chu Minyi, head of the Chinese delegation of the Sino-French Northwest Inspection Team who has just returned to Shanghai, the Northwest, only Xinjiang Province, is 16 times larger than Zhejiang Province. The products are rich and the best in the country. Xinjiang Province is so large that not a single person has been seen lacking food and clothing. After returning to inland areas such as Jiangsu and Zhejiang, beggars were seen everywhere, and the state of poverty was far different from that of the Northwest. As for the development of the Northwest, I feel that the most important work is transportation. The inconvenience of transportation is a major obstacle. Now I feel that there are improvements that can be made to the original three routes to Xinjiang, that is, (1) from Guihua through the Inner Mongolia grasslands to the ancient city of Xinjiang Province. This route has no post stations and is relatively close, but it is more laborious to travel. If you use camels, it will take more than two months. If you use cars, it will only take more than 20 days. However, if you use cars, ordinary cars cannot bear this heavy task, because ordinary cars are very laborious in the desert. The creeping car that was tested this time must be very convenient, but it is too heavy. Therefore, I have planned to improve it according to the method of creeping cars so that it can be applied to this route and facilitate transportation. (2) From Peiping-Xi'an to Lanzhou, via Suzhou and Hami, to reach Dihua, there are a total of five sections on this route, 18 stations each. It usually takes more than 90 days to travel this route. If cars can also be used, it can be reached in 30 days. (3) For those going to southern Xinjiang, they must pass through Suzhou to Haas, which takes four months. In the future, if the transportation in the Northwest can be improved first, development will be easy. Then China's wealth and strength are promising. As for the detailed situation of the inspection of the Northwest, I will have a detailed report at the Central Memorial Week. Although Xinjiang Province is large, the people's races are also quite complex. The most famous are the four races: the Wrapped Head Hui, the Kazakh, the Mongolian, and the Old Jia. (i.e., the Tatar). The people mainly believe in Islam. The Russians have no power there. Because their purpose is opposed to communism, the Soviet Russian red propaganda is completely ineffective.

Japanese Ambassador Shigemitsu Issues a Statement on Sino-Japanese Relations

Denies Mobilization of Japanese Troops

Shanghai, 17th (Dentsu): Ambassador Shigemitsu issued the following statement on Sino-Japanese issues on the afternoon of the 17th. Recently, various unpleasant incidents have occurred between China and Japan, which have aroused public opinion in both countries, which is regrettable. The Nakamura incident is the most unfortunate of these. The Japanese government is seeking practical means to resolve the relations between the two countries in a friendly manner as soon as possible. Although the nature of the Nakamura incident is very serious and sad, it should not be difficult to resolve it quickly if appropriate solutions are sought for this incident alone. Regarding the Nakamura incident, there is a rumor that the Japanese army has a mobilization plan. This is completely groundless and is intended to be promoted.

Sichuan Compatriot Association Asks the National Government to Pay Attention to the Xikang Problem

The Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, considering the increasingly serious issue of Xikang (a region encompassing western Sichuan and eastern Tibet), telegraphed the National Government yesterday, stating: Urgent, To the Nanjing National Government: The Xikang region originally served as a shield for Sichuan Province. We, fearing for our own safety, must first prevent the fall of our neighbor. Recently, instigated by others, the Dalai Lama launched a major invasion of Kang. Although your government dispatched Tang Kesan to prevent it, the effort proved ineffective. Our association has recently received telegrams from various public organizations in Sichuan and Kang, reporting that Tibetan troops have not only failed to withdraw from Ganzi and Zhanhua but have also advanced to peek into Lihua, already occupying the two villages of Qiongxia, and have transported a large number of aircraft and cannons from India, posing a threat to the entire Kang region. According to reliable investigations, some people are commanding the Tibetan troops, and in Doron, under the jurisdiction of Degé, and Eyi Mountain, under the jurisdiction of Enda, which are occupied by the Tibetan army, British people are mining gold. As this concerns national defense and the well-being of Sichuan Province, our association cannot remain silent. We urge your government to immediately telegraph the Sichuan-Kang border defense forces to quickly increase troops to Kang to strengthen the border, and to protest to the British government, forbidding them from further unreasonable interference in Tibetan affairs, and to instruct the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission to formulate a plan for governing Tibet, to seek a fundamental solution, and not to continue procrastinating, thereby harming Kang and the country. The people of Sichuan have suffered greatly from war. Why does the central government leave the 300,000 Sichuan troops unused and listen to a mere Dalai Lama spreading false illusions? For the sake of resisting imperialism and supporting the weak, we hope that you will take action. This is what we expect. Respectfully, The Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai.

Beijing-Pingjin (Beijing-Tianjin) Line Officially Reopens Yesterday

The China National Aviation Corporation's Beijing-Pingjin air route officially reopened yesterday morning. The Beijing-bound plane was originally scheduled to take off from Beijing Station at 8:00 AM yesterday, but it was delayed until 8:50 AM due to waiting for the Beijing-Shanghai night express train to load mail. It was then that pilot Chen Buzhou flew the No. 11 Xuzhou aircraft north to Pingjin Station. The southbound plane took off from Pingjin South at 8:00 AM in the morning, with pilot Zhang Huayi and aircraft No. 7. The Cangzhou plane arrived at Beijing Station at 3:40 PM yesterday. Each station along the line landed to unload mail according to schedule. Because the Tianjin station was still suffering from flood damage, the mail was transferred to Tianjin by the Pingpu train that day. Because yesterday was the first day of the Beijing-Pingjin resumption of flights, the amount of mail carried was very small.

Exhibits from Various Places Arrive in Shanghai for the Road Exhibition

The establishment of the National Road Association began in 1921 (民十). At that time, there was only the Pacific Rim Road Association, in which Westerners accounted for the majority of members. Later, Chinese members believed that there was no need for others to handle Chinese roads on their behalf, and Chinese people should start by planning for themselves. Therefore, Wang Zhengting, Yu Qiaqing, Nie Yuntai, Chen Guangfu, and others came forward to organize the Chinese National Road Construction Association, and hired Wu Shanjun to lead the association's affairs. After ten years of arduous efforts, in order to promote nationwide road and city traffic and expand publicity, a road and city exhibition was specially held in the middle section of Avenue Petain (贝当路) in the French Concession of this city. Completed and uncompleted road maps and charts from all provinces and cities across the country, as well as various models of municipal construction, were collected, all with explanations and separately established. In addition, the most exquisite road and city exhibits from friendly nations such as England, the United States, France, Germany, the Netherlands, Cuba, and Finland were also added. Representatives from the governments of Henan, Tianjin, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces have been reporting their arrivals in recent days, all with detailed charts and various photos of roads and cities, sent to the association for establishment. Yesterday, the Japanese Consul General specially sent Mr. Iijima Masao to the exhibition site to report that the country's road and city exhibits, totaling more than 30 pieces, had been shipped to Shanghai and requested space. He will send staff and craftsmen to the venue tomorrow morning to renovate the exhibition hall site, and has been given entry badges by the site staff to allow them to transport them to the exhibition to learn from each other and facilitate progress.

Prevention of Cholera Report No. 8

The National Maritime Quarantine Service issued Prevention of Cholera Report No. 8 yesterday, stating: (1) The cholera situation in the week from September 5 to 12 was roughly the same as the previous week. There were 30 cases of cholera in the Chinese area, with 2 deaths; 27 cases in the International Settlement, with 4 deaths; and 4 cases in the French Concession, with no deaths. In total, there were 61 cases and 6 deaths. From all aspects, the discovery of mild cholera cases seems to have reached its peak. We can expect it to gradually disappear in the near future. (2) On the 7th of this month, the quarantine medical officer at the Niuzhuang seaport discovered a 13-year-old child suffering from cholera on the "Taili" (Chinese) ship. This ship carried 97 passengers and 52 sailors and was departing from Tianjin. After all personnel on board underwent injections, the passengers were transferred to the Niuzhuang Seaport Quarantine Station. After five days of isolation, they were immediately released. It is strange that this child suffering from cholera came from Tianjin, as this disease has not occurred in that port. (3) News came from Wuhu that on the Wusong ship, which departed from Shanghai to Hankou on the 12th of this month, a cholera patient was discovered on the 14th of this month. Although it has not been confirmed as cholera by bacterial examination, the quarantine officer stationed in Hankou has, for the sake of prudence, administered injections to all passengers before they disembarked. (4) Millions of refugees from the disaster areas are still being transported to Shanghai. Special attention is being paid to their health before they leave Hankou and after they arrive in Shanghai. Quarantine officers board all ships arriving at the wharves to administer preventative injections to everyone and issue certificates. Those who are missed in Hankou are injected in Nanjing, and a final inspection and injection are carried out in Wusong. We are doing our best to reduce infectious diseases to a minimum and to prevent Shanghai from being infected. (5) Although the cholera epidemic in Shanghai is not serious, we still plan to administer preventive injections to those going to Hankou, Qingdao, Dalian, Japan, Hong Kong, and various ports in the south for the convenience of health officials in various places. The Japanese authorities have ordered that those traveling on Japanese ships must have their injections checked. If all on board have been injected, this measure seems unnecessary. (6) Along the Yangtze River ports, more people seem to be dying from dysentery and typhoid fever than from cholera. After cholera is brought under control, our second step will be to prevent dysentery and typhoid fever. (7) In Wusong, the injections for passengers going to Ningbo stopped on the 15th of this month. Since the work began on August 2, a total of 33,389 people have been injected.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Bans Vendors from Tapping into Shop Electricity

1. Must Report to the Company

2. Must Modify Equipment

Many street vendors use electricity from nearby shops for business at night. The Municipal Public Works Bureau has not prohibited such actions, which violate the electricity company's regulations, out of consideration for the livelihoods of the vendors. However, it has been found that the electrical equipment used by these vendors is mostly decayed and unsafe, posing a risk of electric shock if not handled with care. For the sake of public safety, some restraint must be exercised. Therefore, four regulations have been stipulated: (1) Electricity users who supply electricity to vendors must first report the names of the vendors and the number of lamps used to the electricity company. Those who have already done so should make a supplementary report. (2) All electrical equipment connected to the vendors must use outdoor installation methods, capable of withstanding wind and rain. (3) The wires connected to the vendors must be at least 2.5 meters above the ground. (4) All existing electrical equipment of the vendors must be modified in accordance with the provisions of items (2) and (3) before November of this year. A fine of two yuan per lamp will be imposed for overdue modifications, and they will be ordered to make the modifications. Before being qualified, users must not allow them to use electricity. Otherwise, if found, the user's current will be cut off. It is reported that the order has been communicated to all electricity companies for notification and will be announced to all vendors and shops that provide electricity to vendors for compliance.

Baoyu Lane Tenants Oppose Rent Increase

The tenants of Baoyu Lane (寳裕里), Caishi Street (菜市街), French Concession, opposed the landlord's desire to increase the rent again and held a general meeting of all tenants at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday (the 16th). All the tenants of the lane participated unanimously and publicly elected Mo Qichang as chairman. The meeting was conducted with due ceremony. The chairman first reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that the rent for the lane was previously only 18 yuan per building. After the new houses were built, the rent suddenly increased to 60 yuan. At that time, the tenants appealed for a reduction, and the landlord promised not to increase the rent again. Only two years have passed, and now a notice has been suddenly issued that the rent for the lane will be uniformly increased by 30% from November 1. At a time when the provinces are reporting floods and the Shanghai commercial market is sluggish, our tenants are already worried about making ends meet with the current rent, how can they bear further burdens. It has been found that the landlord, Dehe Foreign Firm (德和洋行), has always been known for its benevolence and trustworthiness, but now it is increasing the rent by a huge 30% (i.e. 18 yuan), which is truly unbearable. With the date of the rent increase approaching in the blink of an eye, our tenants should jointly plan a countermeasure. It was decided to send a letter to the landlord, Dehe Foreign Firm, based on the above reasons and facts, requesting them to withdraw the order to increase the rent and to discuss further actions after receiving a reply.

Call for Articles for the 60th Anniversary Supplement of This Newspaper

Now that this newspaper is commemorating its 60th anniversary, we are specially publishing a commemorative supplement, both to increase social interest in discussing issues and to reward our readers for their enthusiastic support of this newspaper. Starting in October, it will be published once a week, covering dozens of topics such as world affairs, politics, economics, and society. The titles of the first ten issues of the supplement are listed as follows. We respectfully hope that scholars and experts in the country will contribute their valuable articles to enhance our publication and benefit the world.

World China Shanghai Transportation

Economy Water Conservancy Education Overseas Chinese

Northeast Science

Guidelines for Submissions

1. Submissions must be within the scope of the topics predetermined by this publication.

2. Before submitting an article, contributors should first request a form from the 60th Anniversary Supplement Department of this newspaper and mail it to us for special arrangements in order to avoid duplication.

3. The language should be popular and lively, and the writing must be clear and punctuated.

4. If the submission is a translation, please attach the original text. If it is inconvenient to attach the original text, please provide detailed information on the original title, author's name, publication date, and location.

5. Submissions that are published will be compensated with a small fee, ranging from three to ten yuan per thousand words.

6. The amount of compensation for published submissions will be determined by this publication and will not be discussed in advance. If contributors wish to set their own amount, please indicate this when filling out the form.

7. The copyright of published submissions belongs to this publication.

8. This publication may make appropriate additions and deletions to submissions, but contributors who do not wish others to make changes may indicate this when filling out the form.

9. To request a form, please write to the 60th Anniversary Supplement Department of the Shen Bao (申報) Newspaper in Shanghai.

Reader Correspondence

Mr. Someone's Inquiry

I was about to graduate from a traditional middle school when, due to economic pressure, I dropped out midway. In recent years, I have been traveling around, holding a position in the political world. In reality, it was just mingling on the surface as a very minor official. Seeing the dignity and pompous airs of those "masters," it was truly unbearable. To put it impulsively, I should have packed my bags and left immediately. However, for the sake of eating, I had to suppress my temper and look up to others. I thought that if things continued like this, I would not get any material benefits, but I would feel very mentally distressed. Gentlemen, I am ashamed to say that I have no other skills besides holding a pen. Changing careers? Considering which job I could do, I pondered it over and over in my mind, unable to make a decision. Finally, with the partial understanding of my brother, I came up with a method: to raise some money, choose a place near the city, buy a few acres of garden land, build a few thatched houses, grow some vegetables and fruits, and raise chickens and ducks to live the life of a farmer. I would not be dependent on others, and I could endure the hardship. However, I am a complete layman when it comes to gardening. If I ask the gardeners for advice, they rely entirely on experience, which cannot be verbally transmitted. It seems that long-term practice is necessary. My current job cannot be left for a moment. If I quit it to practice planting, my whole family would starve. This is absolutely impossible. I wonder if there is any shortcut to learning. I feel that apart from such self-reliance, there is nothing else in the world that I can do. Is this ideal feasible after all? I sincerely seek your guidance.

(Reply) Mr. Someone, we admire your letter very much. Who else should lead a life other than one of self-reliance? Because you can still endure hardship, you want to be independent and think of gardening. We fully agree and hope that you make a resolution to follow this plan. The first step may be to investigate gardening books, first investigate the bibliography, then purchase them. Then, visit experts. We hope you do not underestimate the gardeners. Their experience is our most valuable teacher. At the same time, you must start a practical trial. However, it is best to delay leaving your current job. In case the initial trial fails, it will be even more difficult to make a living. You must be cautious about this point. Unfortunately, we do not know you in detail, and this is all we can offer. Please forgive us.

Mr. Xin Sun's Inquiry

I am a thirty-year-old young man, working in a small bank near Shanghai. I also bear the economic pressure in my family. However, my interests are not very close to commercial affairs, especially the banking industry. I have been forced to make do for ten years, and have suffered from severe neurasthenia. The doctor also said that I need to change my profession. Sir, based on my desires and symptoms, the only way is to leave my current job. But how can I solve the economic problem? What I like is a profession close to literature or a specialized field, with the possibility of continuous progress and research, such as a reporter, secretary, bookstore, or library staff. But how can I necessarily get it? I know that you can only give discussions and guidance on the issue, and cannot provide practical assistance universally. I hope you will publish this article for me, so that people know that a profession must be close to one's own talent and cannot be forced. On the one hand, I also hope that there will be people who sympathize with me and provide practical assistance!

(Reply) A profession must be close to one's talent. This is the principle of job selection. However, since you already have a job, you may as well pursue your favorite studies in your spare time (as you say, it is a literary kind of study). This is also a special way for those who have a job to study. Because there is a kind of thing that is close to talent that cannot be used as a profession, this can take care of both sides. It is not appropriate to leave your current job easily.

Mr. Wang Boming's Inquiry

Boming is only twenty-three years old this year, and has been teaching for a full seven years. In the middle, he has experienced all kinds of difficulties, tasted all kinds of hardships, and the situation has changed. It is hard to express in a word. First, he suffered the pain of dropping out of school, then he suffered from the torment of illness, and now he is suffering from the oppression of life. His mind and energy are exhausted. How can he make a living? I thought that when I was young, I had strong aspirations and never thought of working hard to make a difference, fulfilling the responsibility of a member of the nation, and seeking the happiness of a line in society. But when I was only nine years old, my kind father passed away, and my family had no wealth. I could not finish my studies. Thanks to my virtuous mother, who sold her hairpins to buy books. However, a child without a father is lonely and helpless. In important places of schools, there is no money and no one. After graduating from elementary school, middle school is as strict as a chasm. Although I have the ambition to reach high positions, I am ultimately reduced to dropping out of school. Whenever I see others carrying baskets and books, running around in Shanghai and Suzhou, walking with high spirits, I cannot help but cover my face and weep, and sigh that my fate is not as good as theirs. Alas, if I had more money, I would go from middle school to university, and even study in Europe and the United States, breathe new air, and study new sciences. Wouldn't it be as easy as turning my hand to become a master, doctor, engineer, senior professor, or university president? Why would I be so frustrated in the world, unable to make ends meet? Alas, now it is over. Since Ming dropped out of school, he was fortunate to have the help of his father's friend, who recommended him to a certain elementary school as an assistant teacher, earning sixty or seventy yuan a year. He dared not use it to provide for his parents, but only to make up for the lack of food and clothing. At that time, ashamed of his superficial knowledge, he recited and chanted from dawn to dusk, with a diligence hundreds of times greater than the students. As a result, his body underwent major changes, and his thin bones were fragmented and his arms could not be grasped. Although he has recovered and is as strong as ever, he is still trapped by his qualifications, barely passing every year. And the situation is unstable, the economy is difficult, and the teaching fees are owed for more than ten periods. Making a living is difficult, and living is difficult. My old mother is old, and my weak wife and young sisters, although they do not say they are crying from hunger and cold, are still wearing tattered clothes and eating coarse food. This is close enough. Is this the fate of my elementary school teacher? Why is it so difficult? If I do not find another way, can I still maintain family life in this troubled world? A crucian carp in the West River, a soul in a cauldron, is the future imaginable? Therefore, I sincerely ask the gentleman for help, or bestow valuable advice, so that it can be used as a compass. I am very grateful. I also hope to reply in the newspaper, then my colleagues in the elementary school world will be even more grateful. How can only those who have dropped out of school weep and thank you!

(Reply) Life is difficult, and all parties are the same. You only feel that masters, doctors, professors, etc. have high positions and a lot of money. As far as we know, they feel a lot of material pressure and mental pain. There are also many people who have big titles and are unemployed. The bigger the title, the more helpless. First, I advise you not to envy them. You have two advantages: (1) As you said, your fragmented and thin bones are now as strong as ever, which is a very gratifying thing. (2) You are fortunate to have a job, although the annual income is meager, it is better than nothing. You should strive to supplement your knowledge and skills in your spare time. If you can improve your knowledge and skills step by step, then the opportunities for excellence will be more and more every day. The more you feel the difficulty of life, the more you strive to improve your knowledge and skills. I don't know how many great educators, both Chinese and foreign, started as elementary school teachers. Please do not be discouraged. Changing careers is not a proper and not a stable way. I hope you think twice.

Local News Two

Eight-Year-Old Boy Dies a Miserable Death, Bound with Stones and Sunk to the Bottom of the Huangpu River

Not an Ordinary Kidnapping Case

A Scene of Murder for Money

Zhu Songlin Cannot Deny It

Yao Zhusheng Still Tries to Evade Responsibility

Yao Gu's eight-year-old son, Jiusheng, who lives at No. 199 Ma'an Lane, Chongqing Road, a widow living at her door, was playing at the entrance of his grandmother Gu Zhao's house at No. 96 Taiwei Lane, An'an Road, at 3:00 p.m. on July 7 this year, when he was suddenly abducted by bandits and disappeared without a trace. Later, because the ransom of 20,000 yuan was not successful, he was torn up and Jiusheng was thrown into the Huangpu River and buried in the belly of a fish. Jin Chunwu, the Chinese detective of the Jing'an Temple Police Station, etc., had arrested Zhu Songlin (i.e. Xu Miaogen), the principal offender in the case, a native of Pudong, the suspect, a Suzhou woman, Lu Wang, and the abettor, Yao Zhusheng (i.e. Zisheng, the head of the victim's clan), a local, and sent them to the First Special District Court for interrogation. The details of the case have been reported in this newspaper twice. Now, it is learned that according to the interrogation situation, this case is not an ordinary kidnapping case, but a case of murder for money in order to seize the family property.

The Truth About Jiusheng's Murder After the last court hearing was postponed, the Chinese and Western detectives repeatedly interrogated the captured Zhu Songlin in order to understand the truth. Zhu then confessed that Yao Jiusheng was actually killed by him. After Zhu met Yao Zhusheng, Yao entrusted Zhu to find a way to harm Yao Gu. Zhu then lured Jiusheng out and first hired a car from Dahua Motor Company at the intersection of Gordon Road and Avenue Haig, drove to Huishan Wharf, abandoned the car and boarded a sampan, ferrying to Sanlintang, Pudong, intending to temporarily lodge there. Later, Zhu was deeply afraid of being discovered by the local Public Security Bureau, and also afraid that Yao Jiusheng would reveal the truth, so he wanted to take Jiusheng back to Shanghai. At this time, Zhu suddenly had the intention of murdering. He found a large stone, a hemp rope, and hired a sampan again, drove to the center of the river, tied the large stone to one end of the rope, and tied the other end to Jiusheng's body, pushing him into the river, causing him to sink to the bottom of the Huangpu River. The corpse could not be salvaged. At that time, Zhu took out one yuan from his side and gave it to the boatman, telling him not to publicize it. He took off a pair of shoes that Jiusheng was wearing in advance as a proof for the future ransom. Then he returned to Shanghai alone. Later, because the ransom was not successful, he threw the shoes in the alley outside No. 257 Chongqing Road. The Chinese and Western detectives obtained the confession, and then supervised Zhu Songlin to go together and found a pair of shoes.

Statement by the Police Lawyer Yesterday afternoon, the date for the continued hearing of the case arrived. Around 2:00, Yao's family's male and female relatives and neighbors all came to the Second Criminal Court of the Special Court to listen, about hundreds of people, causing the court to be full and crowded. Yao Jiusheng's biological mother, Yao Gu, sat silently in the audience, her eyebrows locked in spring mountains, crying non-stop. At 2:30, Judge Wu Tingqi took the seat, first interrogating a misappropriation case. When the interrogation involved this case, it was already after 4:00. The defendant Yao Zhusheng hired two lawyers, Tao Wuzhi and Yu Hualong. Lu Wang hired Wang Liangqing as a lawyer to defend him. Only Zhu Songlin had no lawyer to represent him. First, the police lawyer Wang Yaotang stood up and stated the details of the case in detail, saying that after Yao Jiusheng was abducted, his family posted advertisements to look for him, initially offering a reward of 100 yuan, and later increasing it to 500 yuan. A total of 15 letters of extortion were received from the bandits. Yao Gu had paid the bandits 20 yuan. However, regarding the second defendant, Lu Wang, according to Zhu Songlin's confession, she had nothing to do with this case, and was actually framed on purpose. Therefore, he asked to be sentenced first, so as to avoid detention of the innocent. Now there are witnesses in the case, please interrogate them, and then present the letters and shoes for inspection.

The Accent of a Pudong Person According to Gu Quansheng, a driver of Dahua Motor Company, on July 7, at more than 2:00 p.m., the defendant Zhu Songlin brought a woman and a boy about seven or eight years old to hire a car. I drove car No. 17555, first saying that the fare to the Bund was one yuan, and then suddenly wanted to go to Huishan Wharf. The car arrived at Tilanqiao, and Zhu et al. got off, giving me one and a half yuan for the fare and half a yuan for the wine money. At that time, Zhu personally wrote one yuan and five cents on the signature paper, and then presented the signature paper to the case. But the so-called woman is not the defendant Lu Wang, etc. According to Gu Peiheng, he is an assistant at lawyer Jiang Jishi's office. Yao Gu is my sister. After my nephew Jiusheng was abducted, he first received two letters, demanding a ransom of 20,000 yuan. Later, he suddenly received a phone call from the bandits, which I answered. He asked me if I had received the letter and what to do now. I replied that the letter had been received and would be implemented according to the letter. However, I observed that his accent was very similar to that of the former tenant, Zhu Songlin. Because I live at No. 96 Taiwei Lane, An'an Road, Zhu came to rent my house in March this year and lived there for more than a month before moving elsewhere. He is a native of Pudong, so his accent is very easy to distinguish, etc.

Zhu Songlin's Confession According to the woman Xu Zhang, Zhu Songlin is my husband. He also has a concubine named Zhou Juxian. Since Zhu took a concubine, I have disagreed with him and separated. I have also heard Juxian and Zhu Songlin talk about Yao Jiusheng being killed by her husband. However, I do not know how he was murdered. It has been found that Zhu Songlin's real name is Xu Miaogen. Because he was raised in the Zhu family, he changed his name. Questioning Zhu Songlin confessed that in 1927, I had a dispute with my friend Zhang Shaorong in Hankou over opium, and Zhang and Lu Wang's husband, Lu Rensheng, embezzled 1,000 yuan from me. Therefore, I filed a lawsuit in the Xiaokou Court. I was detained for three years, and then released to Shanghai. This case has nothing to do with Lu Wang. It was because her husband embezzled my money that she framed me. As for Yao Zhusheng, I met him in Hankou before. At that time, Yao opened a small You Tiantian restaurant. I have no grudges with him. On February 29 this year, I came to Shanghai from Pudong and met Yao at the entrance of Baoyu Lane. Seeing that my clothes were ragged, he gave me two yuan and made an appointment to meet at a Yile Tian teahouse. He then entrusted me to find a way to seduce Yao Gu and give me 120 yuan. Later, because I saw that Yao was gentle and kind-hearted, I could not bear to harm her. However, Yao Zhusheng repeatedly discussed it, saying that since the seduction was a failure, it would be better to lure away her son. I followed him, lured Jiusheng out. That night, because I could not meet Yao, I took Jiusheng to Pudong. He accidentally fell into the Huangpu River. I really did not use large stones and ropes to tie him to Jiusheng's body to murder him. I got a total of 220 yuan from Yao Zhusheng, etc.

The Case Was Postponed for Another Hearing The rest of the confessions were the same as the last time and have been reported in the newspaper, so they are omitted. Judge Wu checked the confessions and threw the 15 letters down and asked Zhu to read them, asking how many of them were written by you. Zhu looked at them for a long time, and then took out three letters that were not written by him. He admitted that the remaining ten letters were written by him. There were also two letters that were written by a fortune-telling stall in Hankou on his behalf. Lu Wang denied the accusations, and Yao Zhusheng still confessed that he was framed by Zhu. Judge Wu said that it was late, and ordered that the case be postponed to October 1 at 2:00 p.m. for another hearing. Lu Wang was released on bail, and Zhu and Yao were returned to custody.

Two Kidnappers in the Wang Zenshi Case Executed by Firing Squad

Chen Xinggen, 32, a kidnapper from Shanghai, and He Yuren, 28, from Muxian, were arrested by the French Police for jointly forming a gang to kidnap Wang Zhenshi, the young owner of Wang Yutai Tea Shop, with weapons, and were sent to the French Concession Public Concession, where they were sentenced separately. Lu Liankui, the Chinese Chief Inspector of the Public Concession Police, found that Chen and He had committed two cases of kidnapping Lin Weiqing, the elder brother of Lin Biao, the President of the Jiangsu High Court, and Chen Mingsheng, the compradore of Merril and Co., and extorting ransoms in the Public Concession. Therefore, he brought the two criminals for trial at the First Special Court and confirmed that they were true. Chen and He were sentenced to death and submitted to the Provincial Government for approval. Yesterday afternoon was the date of execution. Judge Cheng Shangfeng opened the court and ordered the two criminals to be brought to the case, asking if they had any last words. Chen Xinggen requested to send a letter to No. 10 Tongzhou Road, ordering his mother to collect the body. He said he had no words. Judge Cheng then allocated two yuan to the two criminals to buy food and drink, and then the police escorted them to the Caohejing execution ground by car, where the police executed them by firing squad.

Hand Grenades and Steel Pipes Seized

Whether They Were Commissioned by the Jinling Manufacturing Plant

Must Be Investigated Before a Decision Can Be Made

At about 1:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, the Harbin Police Station received a report from Ren Runsen, a representative of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Wu Pu, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, saying that Chen Xunzhi, a Guangdong native living at No. 627 Yuanhe Lane, Wuzhou Road, was a reactionary element and privately hid military supplies, etc., and requested cooperation in the arrest. The head of the police then sent the Chinese detective Hou Fulin and the Western detective MacLellan to go to the address to arrest Chen. After searching, nothing was found. After questioning, it was learned that he was an accountant at Yongguang Electric Manufacturing Factory at No. 362 on the same road. They went to the factory and found a lot of small white steel pipes (about two inches long) needed for military supplies, which were parts of the hand grenade. They were taken into custody by the detectives, and Chen was taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to the police lawyer Zhang Tianyin's statement of the case, it was stated that the investigation revealed that Yongguang Electric Manufacturing Factory had a contract with the capital Jinling Arsenal to manufacture this item, and it was not privately made. Moreover, a foreman surnamed Shen in the factory had previously been detained for stealing models and sent to the Simple Court of Justice. Although he was declared innocent, there was also a case to be checked. The police must have conclusive evidence to present that this item was supplied to which party. If this kind of supplies should not be manufactured in the concession, the police may prosecute the court. They also presented the white steel pipe for inspection. Then Ren Runsen, a representative of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, reported the matter again and requested a transfer. Wu Pu, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, also stated that the factory's main gate was closed all day, and the staff and workers all entered and exited from the back door, so there was a suspicion of reactionary work. He also described various suspicions. When questioned by the defendant, he confessed that he was an accountant in the factory. The manager's surname was Li, and he was not currently in Shanghai. This kind of white steel pipe was indeed made by the Jinling Arsenal according to the contract. He will present the case. Li Junyou, a native of Ningbo, testified that he opened the Yida Hardware Store at No. 103 Broadway and was also a shareholder of the factory. Since the central government was established in the capital, he had contacted the Jinling Arsenal to contract to manufacture the white steel pipe and steel needle cover, etc., which were parts of the hand grenade. A lot was manufactured every month. The small steel pipes stored in the factory were all returned because the previous sizes did not match. The front door of the factory was always closed because the engineer Shi Yunshi had taken the models privately and a dispute occurred, so it was closed. He also stated that the defendant was not a reactionary element and asked the court to be clear. After Judge Shen Bingrong checked the confessions, he ordered the Municipal Party Department representative Wu Pu to quickly send a telegram to the Jinling Arsenal to reply. He then ordered that the case be investigated and handled after the Public Security Bureau presented conclusive evidence. The hearing was postponed, and the defendant was returned to custody.

Part of the Third Civilian Residence Completed

160 Residences and 1 Auditorium Completed

The Management Bureau Orders Nearby Poor Households to Register and Move In

The Municipal Government is promoting both the banishment of straw sheds and the construction of civilian residences in this city, striving to gradually banish straw sheds, and civilians will have safer, more hygienic, and cheaper residences. Since the plan was determined, the civilian residences that have been built and completed successively have the first and second residences, a total of 500 rooms. The management of the residences has been in charge of specialists sent by the Social Affairs Bureau, and the results are remarkable. The third civilian residence was planned in February this year by the Civilian Residence Committee and was built in Tanjiazhai, and was reported to the Municipal Government for record. The original plan of the residence was to build 290 rooms and an auditorium. Now it is learned that the first phase of the project, 160 rooms and the auditorium, was completed at the end of August and taken over by the Social Affairs Bureau. The bureau has temporarily appointed Xin Juexian as the administrator of the residence. The rent for each room has also been determined to be two yuan and five cents per month. Yesterday, the Social Affairs and Finance Bureaus posted a notice, ordering the residents of nearby straw sheds to start registering and move in immediately, and ordering the Municipal North Tax Collection Office to collect one month's rent from the residents when they move in, and then collect it monthly. As for the remaining 130 rooms, construction will begin as soon as the original straw sheds nearby are moved away.

The British Police Department Scheduled to Continue Hearing

Record of the Zhu Yanqing Kidnapping Trial

Zhu Yanqing, aged 27, son of Zhu Baoyuan, the owner of Zhenhe Tea Shop at No. 127 Dean Lane, Pentang Lane, North Shanxi Road, Public Concession, Zhejiang Haining native, was kidnapped on the 8th of this month at 11:00 PM. He was taking a chartered car from the tea shop back to his residence at No. 94 Zhaofang Lane, behind the Republican Theater on Fangbanqiao in the Chinese area. While passing in front of Bu Lin Li at the intersection of Zhengjia Muqiao Street and Minguo Road in the French Concession, he was abducted by bandits and hidden in the attic room of No. 73 Jianye Li, Fulv Li Road. They intended to extort a large sum from his family for his release. However, the case was discovered by Jin Jiulin, Detective Inspector of the Special Agency of the French Police, along with detectives Li Yaolong, Tang Yunqing, deputy detectives Qian Yumin, Mao Jinge, Lü Zhulin, Zhang Ziying, etc. On the morning of the day before yesterday at 10:30 AM, they led a team of detectives and rushed to the location, rescuing the hostage and arresting twelve male and female kidnappers from Tongzhou: Zheng A'er, Yu Aqing, Tang Afu, Cao Zhangshi, Qian Taoyuan, Hong A'gen, Lu Yisheng, Wang Ziqing, Wang Jiangshi, Qian Liushi, Liu Shaoqing, and Qian Wangshi. They confiscated two loaded handguns, fourteen lead bullets, one iron chain, and one pair of black-rimmed tortoiseshell glasses with white lenses. They were taken into custody for interrogation, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, the police summoned the victim Zhu Yanqing, and witnesses Gao Zhensheng and Chen Jinfu to the court. The defendants were sent to the Second Special District Court, where Judge Luo Renji and Prosecutor Ding Shikui presided over the criminal court for questioning. First, Gu Shouxi, the police lawyer, explained the case, stating that the defendants had kidnapped Zhu Yanqing by first renting a car and driving it to a remote place, where they forced the driver out and tied him up before kidnapping the hostage. This case was serious, and the police investigation was not yet complete. He requested a postponement of three weeks for a detailed investigation. Detectives Mao Jingen and Lü Zhulin, who were handling the case, reported the circumstances of the breakthrough. They stated that the case began with defendants Wang Ziqing and Wang Jiangshi renting a car, driving it to an open area, and forcing the driver out, tying him to the ground. Then, they went to Zhengjia Muqiao Street to kidnap Zhu Yanqing. After the incident, the Western Detective Chief ordered a strict investigation. At 10:30 AM yesterday, they first arrested the first defendant, Zheng A'er, at No. 13 Jianye Li. When asked about the location of the hostage, he said it was at No. 73. They went upstairs to No. 73 and saw the second, third, fourth, and fifth defendants sitting at the entrance of the attic, looking frightened. When they pushed open the attic door, they saw that the doors and windows were covered with curtains. The victim, Zhu Yanqing, immediately said, "I am the god of wealth, don't shoot!" and was rescued, and the defendants were arrested. Handguns, iron chains, glasses, etc. were confiscated. According to the defendants, the mastermind of the case was Lu Yisheng, the victim's former chauffeur of three years. He was arrested at Huili in Simalu. Detectives were sent to guard the bandits' den, and three more people arrived and were arrested. The confiscated handguns, etc. were presented as evidence. The victim, Zhu Yanqing, stated that he was taking a chartered car at night and, while passing in front of Bu Lin Li at the intersection of Zhengjia Muqiao Street and Minguo Road, where the houses were recessed, he was suddenly surrounded by bandits who showed him handguns. At first, he mistakenly thought it was a police checkpoint, but when the chartered car was overturned and he fell out, he was kidnapped and put into a car. There were people watching him on both sides. The car went west along Minguo Road to Milu Road, then from Nanyang Bridge to Tangjiawan on Lanwei'ai Road, and then from Father Lao's Road, passing Fa Park to the intersection of Qiqi Road and Fulv Li Road, where he got out of the car. He walked into Jianye Li, first to No. 13, and then, after about ten minutes, to No. 73, where he was locked up in the attic until the detectives came to rescue him. He often saw the second, third, and fourth defendants guarding him in shifts. The witness Gao Zhensheng stated that he was a driver at Yun'an Motor Company on North Sichuan Road. On the evening of the 8th at 7:55 PM, two people, a man and a woman, came to rent a car. After an agreement was made, the accounting department ordered me to drive. They said they were going to the 16th pier and then to Avenue Albert. First, we went to the 16th pier and stopped for ten minutes, then to Avenue Albert. After about ten minutes, two people came up and forced me out and tied me up. They drove the car away. The witness Chen Jinfu testified that he drove the chartered car for the victim's family. After the owner was kidnapped, I reported to the police. After hearing this, the official asked each defendant their name, age, address, and origin, and then ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody, pending further trial on October 8.

Zhao Ji Rubber Tube Factory's Lawsuit with Lihe Over Machine Purchase

Machines Purchased That Cannot Operate

Lihe Blames the Workers

Zhao Ji Rubber Tube Factory at No. 71 Haifang Road, in September 1929, ordered rubber tube manufacturing machines from Lihe Foreign Firm on Sichuan Road, with a price of 1,916 British gold pounds. These machines were used to manufacture lead tubes for toothpaste or paint. At the time of ordering, both parties agreed that the machines could produce 15,000 tubes every eight hours and would be delivered within four months. The seller guaranteed that the machines were of the best quality and that their engineers would provide installation instructions. Any disputes should be settled by arbitration, without recourse to the courts. After the machines arrived and were installed, it was discovered that they could not operate. The seller successively sent five engineers to test them, but to no avail. The buyer then stopped paying the installments. When the dispute arose, the seller invited Mr. Kabang, an engineer from Kongshi Foreign Firm, and the buyer invited Mr. Laolai from Jiayang Foreign Firm, to consider and study the situation. In May of this year, Mr. Kabang suddenly withdrew from arbitration duties, and Mr. Laolai ruled that all the machines should be returned to Lihe Foreign Firm, and that the price paid by the buyer should be returned along with compensation for various losses. At this time, Lihe Foreign Firm also filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Shen Zhaoji for failing to pay for the goods. The lawsuit stated that the defendant did not hire skilled workers. After the machine was installed, it was damaged due to the misuse of equipment by unskilled workers, making it difficult to operate. Therefore, the plaintiff was no longer responsible. However, they repeatedly assisted in repairing the machine. The defendant insisted on submitting the matter to arbitration, making it impossible to repair the machine properly. The defendant's arbitrator, on the pretext of the plaintiff's delay in arbitration, suddenly announced that they intended to make a unilateral decision in accordance with English law. Because of the defendant's arbitrator's attitude, arbitration could not proceed. Therefore, they requested the court to make a decision and order the defendant to pay 1,916 British gold pounds, minus the deposit of 3,880 taels that had already been paid. The initial hearing was held on July 6. After both parties presented their case, the plaintiff stated that they would invite a German specialized engineer to Shanghai to install the machines. Today, the engineer has arrived in Shanghai, and Shen Zhaoji is also planning to go to the United States to order other machines. Therefore, Shen's proxy lawyers Ge Zhaoji and Chen Tingrui, and the plaintiff's proxy lawyers Mu Ansu, etc., jointly agreed in the Tenth Court of the Special District Court that the factory would connect to electricity from the power company immediately and test the machines for three days to determine their quality.

Impersonating an Anti-Japanese Association Inspector to Extort Money from a Southern Goods Store

Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

At 4:30 PM the day before yesterday, a young man in a Zhongshan suit suddenly arrived at F康東 (Fu Kang Dong) Southern Goods Store, located at No. 502, half address, Aierjin Road, and asked for Manager Wang. The owner, Fang Yongnian, received him and inquired about his intentions. He claimed to be Chen Rui, from Jiading, and an inspector for the Anti-Japanese Association. He said that according to a secret report from Pan Yuezhang, who recently left the store, the store was secretly importing a large quantity of Japanese goods, which was inappropriate. He requested that a responsible person be sent to the Anti-Japanese Association to resolve the matter, or that fifty Buddhist statues could be offered as a congratulatory gift for a private settlement. Otherwise, there would be unfavorable consequences. Fang Yongnian, upon hearing this, realized that he was a swindler impersonating someone to extort money. He sent Manager Wu Quangen to feign compliance while personally reporting to the local Huisi police station. The police chief ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. Just as they arrived at the entrance of the F康 (Fu Kang) store, Wu Quangen had already handed over forty silver dollars to Chen, who took the money and left the store. He was immediately arrested by the detectives, who found the stolen goods and took him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court, where police lawyer Wang Yaotang presented the case, stating that he was being prosecuted for fraud under Article 370 of the Criminal Code and requested a judgment according to the law. Fang Yongnian and witness Wu Quangen also testified about the events. The defendant Chen Rui claimed that he used to be a teacher. A friend, Pan Yuezhang, had reported to him that the F康 (Fu Kang) Southern Goods Store had recently purchased a large quantity of Japanese goods from Dongtai 洋行 (Yang Hang) in 中虹橋 (Zhong Hongqiao), such as 500 boxes of abalone, 2,500 bags of sugar, and 20 boxes of 味之素 (Ajinomoto), etc. He went to F康 (Fu Kang) yesterday to ask Manager Wang not to import Japanese goods in the future and did not intend to extort money. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the testimony and sentenced Chen Rui to six months of imprisonment for using fraudulent means to obtain money, and the number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed would be deducted from the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. The forty silver dollars were returned to the victim.

Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau Arrests Robbers

Shen Wenda, a detective from the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, learned that Shen Amao and others, the robbers in the case of the Ding family robbery in the Nanyang Jingqiao area under the jurisdiction of the Second Branch of the Third District of Pudong on July 8 of this year, were now hiding in the Dingjiazhai area of nearby Yangjing Town. They sometimes went to the Longquan Teahouse in the town for tea, usually around 8:00 AM every day. He immediately reported this to the captain and requested a quick arrest. The captain, Lu Ying, dispatched detectives Ling Tianpeng, Li Xiaobao, Chen Liangfu, Zhou Peisan, secret agent Li Jinbao, etc., along with informants, and worked with the police chief of the jurisdiction to wait in ambush. They waited until about 9:00 AM yesterday morning, when they saw Shen, the suspect, sitting in the teahouse, chatting and drinking tea. The detectives immediately stepped forward to arrest him and took him back to the team for preliminary interrogation. The suspect confessed directly that in early July, he had conspired with Yang Shaoting, Zhang Zhenfa, and two others to rob the Ding Musheng family in Nanyang Jingqiao with handguns and had spent the stolen money. Furthermore, at 7:00 AM yesterday morning, they arrested Zhang Genfa, another suspect, at No. 1 Zhangjiawan, Pudong, and brought him back to the team for questioning. Zhang also confessed directly. After Lu, the captain, obtained the confession, he immediately prepared a document to be sent to the Judicial Section for further interrogation.

Pedestrian Dies on the Road

Suffering from Acute Cholera

Yesterday, a man passing through Chongfuli on North Sichuan Road in Zhabei suddenly contracted acute cholera, sat on the ground, and rolled around. Residents in the lane gave him medicine and asked his name. He claimed to be Jiang Zhaopei, 37 years old, from Haimen. However, he soon suffered severe abdominal pain, fell to the ground, and died. Witnesses reported it to the police on duty, who reported it to the Second Branch of the Fifth District. The police, unable to find any family members, ordered the local Bao Zhang Fu Liugen to report to the local court for examination.

Anting and Other Towns Build Power Plants

Constructed by Xinzhong Company

Anting, Xugongqiao, and Baihejiang Towns jointly established a power plant in Anting Town. The factory building is now completed. All the machinery and equipment in the factory are made in China by Xinzhong Engineering Company, No. 378 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. The contract was signed yesterday. The prime mover is a cold-gas-powered four-cycle double-cylinder, 45-horsepower, Quanti Shi diesel engine generator, a 30-kai Wei'ai three-phase AC generator. It is expected that power will be generated and light will be provided in about half a month.

Russian Dies of Poisoning

Russian citizen, Naini Yaofei, 31 years old, worked as a watchman. Recently, due to some kind of shock, he secretly took 馬雙齡 (Ma Shuangling) poison the day before yesterday. He collapsed on the road near the intersection of Gongping Road and Broadway. A friend, Derlunskai, who happened to be passing by, saw the situation and hired a rickshaw to take him to Gongji Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective and he died shortly after. The Huishan Police Station was notified and sent detectives to take the body to the Pylon Road morgue. A bottle of Ma Shuangling poison and a few silver dollars were found on his person. The Special District Court sent Prosecutor Guo to examine the body and ordered the Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department to claim the body for burial.

Huaju Film Company's New Film to be Released Soon

Huaju Film Company's new film, "Nine Deaths, One Life," has been completely filmed and will be released in the Central Theater on the 21st of this month.

Huachang Car Company on Avenue Edward will be selling its famous Tiger brand bicycles and painted rickshaws at a 5% discount today. Each purchase will include a special gift from the British Three Guns factory. All revenue from the sales of these two types of vehicles for the entire day will be donated to the Huisheng Charity Society for disaster relief.

Page 20

Youth Corner

Juan's Sorrow

— Zheng Hong

Juan's sorrow is increasing day by day. She has lost her parents. She has lost her hometown. Her hometown is 江北 (Jiangbei), which has now been ravaged by floods. Besides her parents, her family only consists of two younger brothers, who all live in 江北 (Jiangbei). They have some land and can live comfortably. When she received the news of the flood disaster in her hometown, she was very panicked. However, amidst the panic, there was a kind of inexplicable joy. She thought that no matter how much was lost, her parents would be safe and sound. Perhaps they would come to Shanghai safely, and she could be reunited with them. She waited and waited, but later she gradually became disappointed. Not only was there no trace of her parents, but she also had no way of knowing any news about them. There was no acquaintance she could ask, no newspaper she could get any clues from. She, who had been very calm, became distraught. She was flustered and uneasy all day long. But what was the use of this? Her parents were still nowhere to be found.

Every day when the first batch of letters arrived, she was always excited. She would rush out to see if there was a letter for her. After other students excitedly took their letters back, she would slowly walk back empty-handed, dejected and exhausted, as if she had run a long distance. She looked very painful, but she tried her best to control herself and勉强 (reluctantly) said, "There is still no letter from home today. It must be all over." At the same time, as usual, a student would say, "Don't worry. They must have arrived at some safe place early. In the chaos, people often forget everything. It's understandable that they didn't think of writing to you." She would listen to these kinds of words and temporarily treat them as a kind of pointless consolation. However, what comfort did this really give her? The most painful thing in the world is to be in a state of uncertainty.

Her anxiety and irritability gradually disappeared. She became calm, and it was a calmness she had never had before. Often in class, she would sit absentmindedly, with her eyes slightly closed. It looked like she was thinking about her parents. She was thinking about her hometown. We can imagine that she was thinking about how the water flowed everywhere in her hometown, how the water submerged the ripe fields, how the water washed away everything. All of this was what she loved and what she was familiar with. She would also tilt her head from time to time, listening as if she could hear the sound of water. Finally, she saw the tragic situation of her parents. How they climbed onto the roof, crawling and stumbling. How they cried out to the white expanse of water, but there was no rescue. Finally, how hunger and terror forced them. Some were exhausted and dizzy, falling into the water. The others also screamed tragically and jumped down together... She silently, with her eyes closed, shed tears. She didn't even know it until the teacher's occasionally raised voice startled her awake. Then she quickly wiped away her tears and quickly wiped away the teardrops on the book in front of her. She was secretly grieved, but what was the use of this? Her parents were still nowhere to be found.

Last autumn, he came to see his daughter. He was a middle-aged villager with a slightly bald head, wrinkled forehead, sincere smile, and a short, stubby beard. Every move he made showed his sincerity and simplicity. Although he was wearing a silk shirt, the silk shirt was not very suitable for that season, and he also seemed not very used to wearing it. Obviously, he cherished this silk shirt and wore it specially, so as not to wear simple cloth clothes and make his daughter lose face. He sat politely in the reception room, looking at his daughter and chatting about trivial things. Finally, he talked about the bag of raw pearl rice he had brought, saying, "This is what you like to eat. This pearl rice can be cooked in a small pot on a 洋磁風爐 (foreign porcelain stove). There's enough for about five pots. If you want more soup, you can cook it six times... You can share it with your classmates. Are they still good to you?" As he spoke, he carefully took out a bag of sugar. "This is sugar. Don't put too much when you cook it. It's not good if it's too sweet... Be careful not to burn it." This bag of sugar was not what he had brought from the countryside. He had specially bought it after arriving in Shanghai. Later, we saw that it was a bag of high-quality fine white sugar. He wanted to make sure his daughter ate something exquisite. Later, when he was about to leave, as he walked out of the reception room, a breeze blew on his daughter's clothes. He unconsciously pinched her arm and said, "You must wear warmer clothes. Why are the sleeves so short? They must be longer." Unexpectedly, this unconscious pinch caused a classmate who was secretly eavesdropping outside to laugh. He immediately realized it, and his sincere face suddenly turned red. He felt very embarrassed. He felt that he had made a rude gesture, something that only farmers in the fields would do. He carefully looked at his daughter, wondering if she would laugh at him or be embarrassed. Seeing that his daughter was calm and happy, and didn't care at all, he was relieved and left. This deep love deeply moved us, let alone his daughter.

We feel perplexed. How could such a loving parent not give their daughter any news, even in difficult and chaotic times? But where are they after all?

Humor

— Yan Na

Filled with a strong desire for knowledge, I traveled across the ocean from the coastal city of Jia in South China to Shanghai, entering a Western school by the side of the Rihui Harbor. I deeply love nature. The morning and evening sun over the sea and sky, the flying wisps of the waves, the floating seagulls on the waves, and the lone herons in the moonlight are all objects of appreciation. I wish I could embrace them forever and never leave them. I am honored to be listed among the "talents" of the Western school. The first pleasant thing is the natural environment of the Western school, because although it cannot compare to Jia City, it has a different flavor. In front of the school building is a green lawn, and a little further away is a bay of flowing water. Red and purple wildflowers adorn the grassland. The sparse willow forest in the garden constantly emits delicate bird sounds. The spring breeze caresses the face, making people feel intoxicated. I thought to myself, I hope the education of the Western school is as satisfactory as the natural environment. That would fit the old saying, "The spring breeze cultivates people."

The principal is an old celebrity from Jia City, in his forties, with a tall figure and a refined demeanor, naturally possessing the "style" of a celebrity. He is good at writing regulated verse, loves wine, and usually does not attend school board meetings much. He especially detests anniversary weeks because he has to give political reports. Such are the characteristics of a celebrity.

The many faculty and staff hired by the celebrity all have their own expertise. Some are good at coping, and some are good at flattering.

Discussing faculty and staff after class is a common trait of students. Our classmates have always had a harmonious relationship, and when we talk, we are unconstrained by ancient or modern times. One day in May, the weather was clear and bright, a Saturday. After class in the afternoon, we invited many classmates to a mountain in front of the school -- Shanghai has no highlands, clearly just a mound, but stubbornly called it a mountain -- and chose a soft patch of green grass to sit down. We watched the sails on the river, weaving back and forth like a loom. At the junction of the water and sky, a flock of waterbirds scattered and reassembled, soaring in the setting sun. A slight breeze swept over the grass, blowing up waves of wrinkles. The faint sound of a bell broke the silence of the empty sky. Everyone sat in silence for a while. A certain gentleman who loved sports picked up a white stone from the grass, jumped up, and vigorously threw it towards the Western school, shouting, "I want to smash that factory that makes 'manure machines' with one stone!" The stone clanged and landed on a large rock on the hillside. Everyone knew that in his silence, he had thought of the Western school, thought of its chaotic and lifeless way of running the school, and even thought of its celebrity principal, who appeared and disappeared like a divine dragon. Each person's heart burned with intense anger.

Zi Jun, one of the companions, was known for his "humor." His sandalwood-colored face, paired with a pair of bright eyes like copper nails, even when he was silent, had a bit of a funny look. He lowered his head, almost inserting it between his knees. For a long time, he seemed excited. He raised his head, pouted his lips, paused for a while, then bit his lower lip under his upper teeth, supported his chin with one hand, and put on a feminine smile. Everyone knew his story was coming.

"Director, do you know whether the Qin Dynasty came before the Han Dynasty?" Zi Jun put on a delicate, fully feminine, sharp voice, and his eyes even glanced at a companion like shooting stars.

Everyone firmly believed that his talent for imitating people was almost unprecedented and unsurpassed. From his tone of voice and expression, they inferred that he was imitating Ms. Bi, a history and geography teacher. Ms. Bi struggled to teach, as was well known to her students, who "knew their teacher best." But why would she ask such an absurd question? Everyone couldn't help but suspect Zi Jun's deliberate meanness.

Zi Jun looked at everyone's expressions, hesitated for a moment, then stood up in a delicate and charming way, standing in front of us, twisting his neck and looking at everyone, with one hand behind his back and the tip of his tongue licking his upper lip, and said, "The words you asked about, let me go down and look them up in the dictionary and then tell you." All the companions who had taken Ms. Bi's class exclaimed in unison, and people from other classes laughed along.

Amid everyone's laughter, Zi Jun's expression changed again. He put on a layer of sinister and superficial fake smile on his face, and stood for a while, putting on an appearance that seemed dry and arrogant but was actually weak.

Everyone watched Zi Jun's performance in a daze, and couldn't help but exclaim in unison, "Good!" Zi Jun waved his hand, nodded repeatedly, and switched to the expression of Director Ding of the Academic Affairs Office, saying, "Goodbye, I have business in Nanjing. Two months later, I can come here to stay for a few days and investigate." Zi Jun stopped his performance amid the laughter and went off to find pebbles to play with by himself.

Many companions, some were filled with anger, and some could not stop laughing. Ms. T from the same class sat next to me for half a day without saying a word. Now she said in a strange tone, "They deceive us like this, I really don't know how they can bear it." Zi Jun interjected, "To bear what others bear is not what I call bearing." Everyone laughed again.

The twilight was vast and hazy, and the birds had long returned to the forest. The corner of the Western school building was faintly exposed above the jungle. The smoke from the villagers' cooking drifted with the wind, weaving a picture of the unique evening scenery of midsummer. At this time, I painfully felt that the external scenery of the Western school was very beautiful, but it was inevitably "gold and jade on the outside."

Composition Class

— Wei Mei

"Mr. Zhou, when the principal comes, give us a shout." A Yang, afraid of being seen writing a letter by the principal, especially came to smooth things over with Mr. Zhou first.

"Mr. Zhou, when the principal comes, you'd better make a gesture to us -- how about touching your hat?" Wen Yun interjected.

"No, Mr. Zhou, you'd better pinch your nose." He Yu, after reading a book on Wen Hua, looked up and said.

"Oh, don't quarrel..." Mr. Zhou opened his mouth.

"Mr. Zhou, they are very good at quarreling. They don't like to take what's readily available," A Feng opened her mouth.

"A Feng, show me your hand," A Rong shouted in a commanding tone.

"What for?" A Feng said, stretching out her hand.

"Not white at all, I thought you had white hands," A Rong said, looking at it with a smug look.

"Evil carriage (ghost)!" A Feng hit A Rong and sat down to read a novel.

Yu Cao, the star player on the volleyball team, felt bored sitting down and secretly bounced a ping pong ball on the floor.

A Quan was the first to panic and put the book into the desk. Looking back, the principal had not come, so he came over to pinch A Geng. A Geng dodged to the side and knocked over an ink bottle. When A Quan ran over, he knocked off A Yun's dictionary. So A Geng cursed A Quan, and A Yun also hated A Quan. Everything in the classroom was chaotic. Only our Mr. Zhou was still sitting quietly.

Women's Swimming Team

— Bing She

Exploitation

— Zhu Ming

A certain university in Jiangwan can be regarded as an advanced institution among the private universities in Shanghai. Because it has a long history and its performance is not bad, the number of students who go there to study has increased in recent years, so that the school's dormitories are not enough to accommodate them. However, in order to maintain the school's life, the school has to accept more students to increase revenue. All the students who cannot live in the school have to find ways to live outside the school. So there are some speculative investors and businessmen who have built many houses near the school to rent to students. Their vision is really good and their business is really booming. It is said that every school also has the problem of being full, just like the dormitories inside the school. Therefore, houses stand in rows near the school, in addition to dormitories, there are restaurants, all kinds of companies, shops, vendors, and a constant stream of various vehicles, bustling and lively, forming a university market. And the common purpose of this market is nothing more than to exploit students.

The more demand, the more supply should be, this is a simple law of economics. A certain classmate in the school has seen this business of renting houses and cannot help but arouse his desire for profit, thinking that this business is really a good way to get rich. So during the summer vacation, he chose a vacant lot next to the back gate of the school and built a three-story Western-style dormitory. The rooms are larger than those in the school, but the fees charged are much more expensive. At most, the school's dormitory charges only twenty yuan per semester, but this place charges twenty-five yuan, and the facilities are not necessarily better than those in the school. This shows that his exploitative heart is heavy. Sure enough, this classmate's get-rich movement, by the time school started, the rooms had been fully booked. I am a new student who was admitted this semester. I heard that there were no vacancies in the school's dormitory, so I completed a bed in this place before school started and became one of this classmate's employers.

After living in this dormitory for two days, I heard that the rent for this house is not uniform. The rooms facing south are twenty-five yuan, the rooms facing north are twenty-four yuan, and the rooms facing north and close to the toilet are twenty-three yuan. After knowing this method, I really can't help but admire this classmate's clever research on business. Because in this way, both good and bad rooms will have people living in them, and the business will not be affected by the quality of the room's location. This ingenious method has not been thought of and implemented by the school authorities who are good at extracting and the investors and businessmen who are good at profiting. This classmate has thought of it. This is something that the school authorities who are good at extracting and the investors and businessmen who are good at profiting do not know. In the past, the investors, businessmen, vendors, tea boys, and rickshaw pullers who specialized in exploiting students have now come to the point where students are exploiting students. This is probably a progressive phenomenon in university education.

The accommodation fee is collected completely as soon as one moves in, but the electric lights in the dormitory are dim and unclear, and the tap water everywhere does not flow. The toilet is unbearably filthy, making the people living inside feel a lot of unease, but this fellow classmate landlord does not care about it. This kind of behavior of only knowing how to benefit oneself and not knowing how to benefit others makes me unable to help but shout out a few times, "Exploitation, exploitation!" (Moved reward to help disaster relief)
